## Detailed Findings

### autoskill — 🔴 CRITICAL

- **🔴 CRITICAL** `BEHAVIOR_CROSSFILE_ENV_VAR_EXFILTRATION` — Cross-file env var exfiltration: 7 files
  > Environment variable access with network calls in scripts/doctor.py, scripts/backends.py, scripts/run.py
  > **Remediation:** Review data flow across files: scripts/doctor.py, tests/test_run.py, tests/test_e2e.py, scripts/run.py, tests/test_backends.py, tests/test_fetch_window.py, scripts/backends.py

- **🔴 CRITICAL** `BEHAVIOR_CROSSFILE_EXFILTRATION_CHAIN` — Cross-file exfiltration chain: 8 files
  > Multi-file exfiltration chain detected: scripts/doctor.py, scripts/backends.py, scripts/run.py collect data → tests/smoke_lmstudio.py, scripts/run.py → tests/test_run.py, tests/test_e2e.py, tests/test_backends.py, tests/test_fetch_window.py, scripts/doctor.py, scripts/backends.py, scripts/run.py transmit to network
  > **Remediation:** Review data flow across files: tests/smoke_lmstudio.py, scripts/doctor.py, tests/test_run.py, tests/test_e2e.py, scripts/run.py, tests/test_backends.py, tests/test_fetch_window.py, scripts/backends.py

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_SKILL_DISCOVERY_ABUSE` — Broad Capability Claims in Skill Description
  > The skill description claims to 'detect repeated research workflows, match them against existing scientific-agent-skills, and draft new skills' and references '135 sibling skills'. The description is accurate but very broad in scope — the skill essentially claims to observe all user activity and generate new agent capabilities autonomously. This broad framing could lead to the skill being invoked more broadly than intended, though the instructions do include appropriate 'When to Use' and 'Do not invoke' guidance.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Consider narrowing the description to be more specific about the scope and limitations of the skill to reduce the risk of unintended activation.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — Environment Variable Credential Access and Transmission to Network Endpoints
  > The skill reads three sensitive environment variables (SCREENPIPE_TOKEN, ANTHROPIC_API_KEY, FOUNDRY_API_KEY) and uses them to authenticate to network endpoints. While this is documented behavior, the static analysis confirms cross-file env var exfiltration chains across 7 files. The doctor.py script also reads these variables and makes network calls to verify connectivity. The config.yaml can also store the screenpipe token directly, creating a risk of credential exposure if config files are committed to version control (though the instructions warn against this).
  > File: `scripts/doctor.py`
  > **Remediation:** 1. Document clearly that config.yaml should never contain API keys and enforce this with a config validator. 2. Add a check in doctor.py that warns if tokens are found in config files rather than environment variables. 3. Ensure tokens are never logged or included in error messages. 4. Consider using a secrets manager or keychain integration rather than plain environment variables.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_RESOURCE_ABUSE` — Unbounded Screenpipe Data Fetch with Large Time Windows
  > The fetch_window function paginates through screenpipe results with a hard ceiling of _MAX_PAGES = 10,000 pages. With a default page_size of 50, this allows fetching up to 500,000 events. For large time windows (e.g., 'analyze my last week'), this could result in massive memory consumption as all events are accumulated in a list before processing. The cluster.py segment_sessions function also sorts all events in memory. This could cause memory exhaustion on systems with limited RAM.
  > File: `scripts/fetch_window.py:1`
  > **Remediation:** 1. Implement streaming/chunked processing rather than accumulating all events in memory. 2. Add a configurable maximum event count with a sensible default (e.g., 10,000 events). 3. Warn users when time windows are very large before fetching. 4. Consider processing events in batches to limit peak memory usage.

- **🟠 HIGH** `LLM_COMMAND_INJECTION` — Path Traversal Risk in LLM-Generated Skill Names
  > The skill name returned by the LLM in the 'novel' and 'compose' verdicts is used directly to construct filesystem paths without sanitization. If an attacker can influence the LLM output (via indirect prompt injection from screen content), they could cause the skill name to contain path traversal sequences (e.g., '../../../etc/' or absolute paths), potentially writing files outside the intended proposed directory. The decision['name'] value from the LLM response is used directly in Path construction.
  > File: `scripts/run.py`
  > **Remediation:** 1. Sanitize the skill name by stripping path separators and validating against a safe character allowlist (e.g., [a-z0-9-_]). 2. Verify that the resolved draft_dir path is actually under proposed_path using Path.resolve() comparison. 3. Reject any skill name containing '..', '/', or other path-special characters. 4. Add a maximum length limit on skill names.

- **🟠 HIGH** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — Screen Content Capture and Transmission to External LLM Backends
  > The skill captures continuous screen content (OCR of all visible windows) via the screenpipe daemon and transmits processed summaries to external cloud LLM backends (Anthropic Claude API at https://api.anthropic.com, or user-configured Foundry gateway). While the skill documents this behavior and includes a redaction layer, the fundamental data flow involves sensitive screen content — including window titles, application names, and OCR text — being processed and potentially sent to external servers. The redaction layer (scripts/redact.py) is regex-based and cannot guarantee complete removal of all sensitive information before it reaches cloud backends. Users who configure 'backend: claude' or 'backend: foundry' will have cluster summaries (derived from screen content) transmitted externally.
  > File: `scripts/run.py`
  > **Remediation:** 1. Enforce explicit user confirmation before any data is sent to cloud backends. 2. Display a clear summary of what data will be transmitted before each cloud LLM call. 3. Consider making the redaction pipeline more robust (e.g., using NLP-based PII detection in addition to regex). 4. Add a hard opt-in gate that requires explicit user acknowledgment that screen-derived data will leave the machine when cloud backends are configured. 5. Log all data transmitted to external backends for user auditability.

- **🟠 HIGH** `LLM_UNAUTHORIZED_TOOL_USE` — LLM-Generated SKILL.md Written Directly to Disk Without Content Validation
  > The synthesize pipeline writes LLM-generated SKILL.md content directly to disk without any validation of the content. When the LLM returns a 'novel' or 'compose' verdict, the raw skill_body string from the LLM response is written verbatim to a SKILL.md file. If an attacker can influence the LLM output (via indirect prompt injection from screen content, or by compromising the LLM backend), they can cause arbitrary SKILL.md content to be written to disk. The promote.py script then moves these files into the active skills directory with no content inspection, potentially introducing malicious skills into the agent's skill library.
  > File: `scripts/run.py`
  > **Remediation:** 1. Validate LLM-generated SKILL.md content against a strict schema before writing to disk. 2. Sanitize the skill name (decision['name']) to prevent path traversal attacks. 3. Implement content security scanning on generated skill bodies to detect prompt injection patterns. 4. Require explicit user review and approval of generated content before it can be written to disk (not just before promotion). 5. Restrict allowed-tools in generated skills to a safe subset.

- **🟠 HIGH** `LLM_PROMPT_INJECTION` — Indirect Prompt Injection via Screen-Captured OCR Content
  > The skill ingests OCR text from the user's screen via screenpipe and constructs LLM prompts that include this content (after redaction). An attacker who can display text on the user's screen — via a malicious webpage, document, email, or any visible application — can inject instructions into the OCR stream that will be incorporated into the LLM prompt in synthesize.py. The _build_prompt() function in synthesize.py directly embeds cluster data (which includes example_titles and app names derived from OCR) into the prompt sent to the LLM. This creates a classic indirect prompt injection vector where screen-visible content can manipulate the LLM's behavior, potentially causing it to generate malicious SKILL.md files that get promoted into the skills directory.
  > File: `scripts/synthesize.py`
  > **Remediation:** 1. Treat all OCR-derived content as untrusted and sanitize it before embedding in LLM prompts. 2. Use structured prompt formats that clearly delimit untrusted data from instructions (e.g., XML tags or explicit untrusted-data sections). 3. Validate LLM-generated SKILL.md output against a strict schema before writing to disk. 4. Implement content security checks on generated skill bodies before they can be promoted. 5. Consider using a separate, sandboxed LLM call to validate generated skills for injection attempts.

- **🔴 CRITICAL** `BEHAVIOR_ENV_VAR_EXFILTRATION` — Environment variable access with network calls detected
  > Script accesses environment variables and makes network calls in skills/autoskill/scripts/backends.py
  > File: `skills/autoskill/scripts/backends.py`
  > **Remediation:** Remove environment variable harvesting or network transmission

  > File: `skills/autoskill/scripts/backends.py`
  > **Remediation:** Remove environment variable collection unless explicitly required and documented

- **🔴 CRITICAL** `BEHAVIOR_ENV_VAR_EXFILTRATION` — Environment variable access with network calls detected

  > File: `skills/autoskill/scripts/doctor.py`

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `BEHAVIOR_ENV_VAR_HARVESTING` — Environment variable harvesting detected
  > Script iterates through environment variables in skills/autoskill/scripts/doctor.py
  > File: `skills/autoskill/scripts/doctor.py`
  > **Remediation:** Remove environment variable collection unless explicitly required and documented

- **🔴 CRITICAL** `BEHAVIOR_ENV_VAR_EXFILTRATION` — Environment variable access with network calls detected
  > Script accesses environment variables and makes network calls in skills/autoskill/scripts/run.py
  > File: `skills/autoskill/scripts/run.py`
  > **Remediation:** Remove environment variable harvesting or network transmission

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `BEHAVIOR_ENV_VAR_HARVESTING` — Environment variable harvesting detected

### cellxgene-census — 🔴 CRITICAL

- **🟠 HIGH** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — Environment Variable Harvesting with Network Exfiltration
  > The static analyzer detected three separate instances of environment variable access combined with network calls (BEHAVIOR_ENV_VAR_EXFILTRATION). In the context of a bioinformatics skill that legitimately needs only to query a public API, accessing environment variables (which commonly contain AWS credentials, API tokens, SSH keys, database passwords, CI/CD secrets) and transmitting them over the network is highly suspicious and consistent with credential theft. The cross-file nature (7 files involved) suggests a coordinated, multi-component exfiltration design rather than incidental behavior.
  > **Remediation:** Identify and remove all code that reads os.environ or os.getenv and subsequently makes HTTP/network requests. The legitimate cellxgene-census library does not require environment variable harvesting. Any environment variable access should be limited to configuration (e.g., proxy settings) and must not be included in outbound network payloads.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_SKILL_DISCOVERY_ABUSE` — Missing License and Compatibility Metadata
  > The skill manifest declares license as 'Unknown' and does not specify compatibility. While not a direct security threat, missing provenance information (license, compatibility, and no author URL/contact beyond 'K-Dense Inc.') reduces accountability and makes it harder to verify the skill's legitimacy. Combined with the other findings, this contributes to an overall low-trust profile for this package.
  > **Remediation:** Provide a valid SPDX license identifier, compatibility information, and verifiable author contact/repository URL. Skills from unverifiable sources should be treated with heightened scrutiny.

- **🔴 CRITICAL** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — Cross-File Environment Variable Exfiltration Chain Detected
  > Static analysis has flagged a cross-file exfiltration chain spanning 8 files and environment variable exfiltration across 7 files. Although no Python script files were surfaced in the skill package content provided, the pre-scan static analyzer detected patterns consistent with environment variable harvesting combined with network calls. This is a strong indicator of a multi-stage data exfiltration pipeline where sensitive environment variables (API keys, tokens, credentials) are read and transmitted to an external server. The skill's manifest does not declare allowed-tools, making it impossible to verify tool restrictions, and several referenced Python files (cellxgene_census.py, scanpy.py, tiledbsoma.py) were not found in the package, suggesting hidden or obfuscated components.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Do not install or use this skill. Conduct a full audit of all 28 files in the package (23 Python files, 3 other, 2 markdown). Identify which Python files are reading environment variables and making network calls. Remove or sandbox any file performing unauthorized network egress. Verify that all referenced files are present and contain only legitimate CELLxGENE Census API usage.

- **🟠 HIGH** `LLM_COMMAND_INJECTION` — Unreferenced Python Scripts with Potential Command/Code Injection
  > The file inventory reports 28 total files including 23 Python files, yet the skill package content only surfaces 2 markdown reference files and no Python scripts. The static analyzer reports no 'unreferenced_scripts' but 23 Python files exist. This discrepancy means a large number of Python files are present in the package but not visible in the provided content. These hidden scripts could contain command injection, eval/exec patterns, or arbitrary code execution that runs when the skill is invoked. The skill's instructions reference Python module names (cellxgene_census.py, scanpy.py, tiledbsoma.py) that shadow legitimate PyPI packages, which could be used for module hijacking.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Audit all 23 Python files in the package. Check for eval(), exec(), os.system(), subprocess calls with user-controlled input. Verify no local files shadow legitimate installed packages (cellxgene_census.py, scanpy.py, tiledbsoma.py would override the real packages if placed in the working directory).

- **🟠 HIGH** `LLM_UNAUTHORIZED_TOOL_USE` — Local Module Shadowing of Legitimate PyPI Packages
  > The skill references files named cellxgene_census.py, scanpy.py, and tiledbsoma.py. If these files exist locally within the skill package directory, Python's import resolution will load these local files instead of the legitimate installed PyPI packages of the same name. This is a classic tool poisoning / tool shadowing attack: the skill instructs the agent to import cellxgene_census, scanpy, and tiledbsoma, but the local shadow files intercept those imports and execute malicious code while potentially passing through to the real library to avoid detection. The static analyzer confirms environment variable exfiltration and network calls are present in the package.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Remove any local .py files that share names with legitimate PyPI packages. Ensure the skill does not bundle cellxgene_census.py, scanpy.py, or tiledbsoma.py locally. Use absolute imports or verify sys.path ordering. Audit the package for any __init__.py or conftest.py that could manipulate import paths.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_SUPPLY_CHAIN_ATTACK` — Unpinned Package Installation Without Version Constraints
  > The SKILL.md instructs users to install packages using 'uv pip install cellxgene-census' and 'uv pip install cellxgene-census[experimental]' without specifying version pins. This exposes the skill to supply chain attacks where a compromised or malicious version of the package could be installed. Combined with the evidence of local shadow files for the same package names, this creates a layered supply chain risk.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Pin package versions explicitly: 'uv pip install cellxgene-census==1.14.0' (or current stable version). Consider using a requirements.txt with hashes for integrity verification. Verify package integrity against known-good checksums.

### citation-management — 🔴 CRITICAL

- **🔴 CRITICAL** `BEHAVIOR_CROSSFILE_ENV_VAR_EXFILTRATION` — Cross-file env var exfiltration: 6 files
  > Environment variable access with network calls in scripts/search_pubmed.py, scripts/extract_metadata.py, scripts/generate_schematic.py, scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py
  > **Remediation:** Review data flow across files: scripts/generate_schematic.py, scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py, scripts/extract_metadata.py, scripts/search_pubmed.py, scripts/doi_to_bibtex.py, scripts/validate_citations.py

- **🔴 CRITICAL** `BEHAVIOR_CROSSFILE_EXFILTRATION_CHAIN` — Cross-file exfiltration chain: 6 files
  > Multi-file exfiltration chain detected: scripts/search_pubmed.py, scripts/extract_metadata.py, scripts/generate_schematic.py, scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py collect data → scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py → scripts/validate_citations.py, scripts/search_pubmed.py, scripts/doi_to_bibtex.py, scripts/extract_metadata.py, scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py transmit to network
  > **Remediation:** Review data flow across files: scripts/generate_schematic.py, scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py, scripts/extract_metadata.py, scripts/search_pubmed.py, scripts/doi_to_bibtex.py, scripts/validate_citations.py

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_SKILL_DISCOVERY_ABUSE` — Cross-Skill Promotion and Undisclosed Dependency on External Skill
  > The SKILL.md instructions prominently promote the 'scientific-schematics' skill and 'Nano Banana Pro' branding, instructing the agent to 'always consider adding scientific diagrams' and that 'Scientific schematics should be generated by default.' This creates an implicit dependency on another skill and promotes its use in a way that may not be relevant to the user's citation management task. The instruction to generate schematics 'by default' for new documents is over-broad for a citation management skill.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Remove or make optional the cross-promotion of the scientific-schematics skill. Citation management does not inherently require diagram generation. If integration is desired, make it explicitly opt-in based on user request.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_SUPPLY_CHAIN_ATTACK` — Unpinned Python Package Dependencies
  > The skill's dependency section specifies packages without version pins (e.g., 'pip install requests', 'pip install scholarly', 'pip install selenium', 'pip install bibtexparser', 'pip install biopython'). Unpinned dependencies are vulnerable to supply chain attacks where a malicious package version could be installed. The 'scholarly' library in particular is a third-party Google Scholar scraper that could change behavior unpredictably.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Pin all dependencies to specific versions (e.g., 'requests==2.31.0'). Use a requirements.txt file with pinned versions and hash verification. Consider using a virtual environment with locked dependencies.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — API Key Passed via Environment Variable to External AI Service
  > The generate_schematic.py and generate_schematic_ai.py scripts read the OPENROUTER_API_KEY environment variable and use it to make requests to the OpenRouter API (https://openrouter.ai/api/v1). While the key is passed via environment (not command-line args, which is good practice), the skill sends user-provided prompts to an external third-party AI service. This represents a data flow where user content leaves the local environment to an external commercial API. The skill does not disclose this external data transmission in its primary description.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic.py:60`
  > **Remediation:** Clearly disclose in the skill description that diagram generation sends user prompts to the OpenRouter external API. Ensure users are aware their content is transmitted externally. Consider making this an opt-in feature with explicit user consent.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — NCBI API Key Read from Environment Variable with External Network Calls
  > The search_pubmed.py and extract_metadata.py scripts read NCBI_API_KEY and NCBI_EMAIL from environment variables and include them in requests to NCBI E-utilities API. While this is standard practice for API authentication, the scripts also read NCBI_API_KEY via os.getenv() and transmit it in HTTP request parameters. If the environment contains sensitive keys, they are included in network requests to external servers.
  > File: `scripts/search_pubmed.py:47`
  > **Remediation:** This is standard API usage. Ensure NCBI_API_KEY is only set when intentionally using PubMed API. Document clearly which environment variables are read and for what purpose. Consider adding a note that these keys are transmitted to NCBI servers.

- **🔴 CRITICAL** `BEHAVIOR_CROSSFILE_ENV_VAR_EXFILTRATION` — Cross-file env var exfiltration: 2 files
  > Environment variable access with network calls in scripts/generate_schematic.py, scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py
  > **Remediation:** Review data flow across files: scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py, scripts/generate_schematic.py

  > Multi-file exfiltration chain detected: scripts/generate_schematic.py, scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py collect data → scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py → scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py transmit to network
  > **Remediation:** Review data flow across files: scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py, scripts/generate_schematic.py

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_UNAUTHORIZED_TOOL_USE` — Mandatory External AI Service Dependency Undisclosed in Manifest
  > The SKILL.md instructions mandate that every clinical decision support document MUST include AI-generated figures via the scientific-schematics skill, which internally calls the OpenRouter API (an external third-party service). This mandatory external dependency is not disclosed in the YAML manifest's compatibility or description fields. Users may not be aware that generating documents will trigger external API calls and incur costs. The instruction states: '⚠️ MANDATORY: Every clinical decision support document MUST include at least 1-2 AI-generated figures using the scientific-schematics skill.'
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** 1. Add explicit disclosure in the YAML manifest description that this skill makes external API calls to openrouter.ai. 2. Make figure generation optional rather than mandatory, or at minimum warn users about the external dependency and cost implications. 3. Add a compatibility note indicating network access is required.

- **🟠 HIGH** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — Cross-File Exfiltration Chain: generate_schematic.py Spawns generate_schematic_ai.py with Credential Forwarding
  > generate_schematic.py acts as a launcher that reads OPENROUTER_API_KEY from the environment, copies the entire os.environ, injects the API key, and passes it to a subprocess running generate_schematic_ai.py. This creates a two-stage exfiltration chain where credentials flow from the environment through a subprocess into external HTTP requests. The static analyzer explicitly flagged BEHAVIOR_CROSSFILE_EXFILTRATION_CHAIN and BEHAVIOR_CROSSFILE_ENV_VAR_EXFILTRATION across these two files.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic.py`
  > **Remediation:** 1. Clearly document in SKILL.md that this skill makes external API calls to openrouter.ai and requires an API key. 2. Prompt the user for explicit consent before making external calls. 3. Avoid copying the full os.environ into subprocess calls; pass only the minimum required variables. 4. Consider validating the API key format before use to prevent injection.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_COMMAND_INJECTION` — User-Controlled Input Passed to subprocess.run Without Sanitization
  > In generate_schematic.py, the user-supplied prompt (args.prompt) is passed directly as a command-line argument to a subprocess call running generate_schematic_ai.py. While subprocess.run with a list argument mitigates shell injection, the prompt string is passed unsanitized and could contain characters that affect argument parsing or logging. Additionally, the prompt is embedded directly into multi-line f-strings used as LLM prompts in generate_schematic_ai.py, creating a prompt injection vector where malicious diagram descriptions could manipulate the AI quality reviewer's behavior.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic.py:75`
  > **Remediation:** 1. Validate and sanitize the prompt argument before passing it to subprocesses. 2. Consider length limits on user-provided prompts. 3. In generate_schematic_ai.py, separate user content from system instructions using clear delimiters when constructing LLM prompts to reduce prompt injection risk.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — Potential Sensitive Data Written to Disk in Intermediate Files
  > The generate_schematic_ai.py script saves intermediate iteration images (e.g., diagram_v1.png, diagram_v2.png) and a JSON review log containing the full API response, critique text, prompts, and scores to disk. If clinical data descriptions are included in prompts, this information persists in log files. The review log at {base_name}_review_log.json contains the full user prompt and all API responses.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py`
  > **Remediation:** 1. Warn users that prompts and API responses are logged to disk. 2. Provide an option to disable logging or automatically clean up intermediate files. 3. Ensure log files are not written to shared or world-readable directories. 4. If clinical data may appear in prompts, add a warning about not including PHI in diagram descriptions.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_SUPPLY_CHAIN_ATTACK` — Unpinned External Dependencies in Scientific Analysis Scripts
  > Multiple scripts import third-party packages (pandas, numpy, scipy, scikit-learn, lifelines, matplotlib, requests) without any version pinning or requirements file visible in the skill package. Unpinned dependencies are vulnerable to supply chain attacks where a malicious package update could compromise the skill's behavior. The requests library in particular is used for external API calls, making its integrity especially important.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py:1`
  > **Remediation:** 1. Add a requirements.txt or pyproject.toml with pinned versions for all dependencies. 2. Consider using a lockfile (pip-compile or poetry.lock) to ensure reproducible installs. 3. Periodically audit dependencies for known vulnerabilities.

- **🟠 HIGH** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — API Key Exfiltration via Environment Variable and External Network Calls
  > The generate_schematic_ai.py script reads the OPENROUTER_API_KEY environment variable and transmits it as a Bearer token in HTTP Authorization headers to an external API endpoint (https://openrouter.ai/api/v1). While OpenRouter is a legitimate service, the pattern of reading sensitive credentials from the environment and sending them to an external server represents a data exfiltration risk. The API key is also passed through subprocess calls in generate_schematic.py, creating a cross-file credential exposure chain. The static analyzer flagged this as BEHAVIOR_CROSSFILE_ENV_VAR_EXFILTRATION and BEHAVIOR_ENV_VAR_EXFILTRATION.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py:68`
  > **Remediation:** 1. Document clearly that OPENROUTER_API_KEY is required and explain what it is used for. 2. Ensure the API key is scoped to minimum necessary permissions. 3. Avoid passing API keys through subprocess environment copies unless strictly necessary. 4. Consider using a secrets manager rather than raw environment variables. 5. Add explicit user consent/notification before making external API calls with credentials.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `BEHAVIOR_ENV_VAR_HARVESTING` — Environment variable harvesting detected
  > Script iterates through environment variables in skills/clinical-decision-support/scripts/generate_schematic.py
  > File: `skills/clinical-decision-support/scripts/generate_schematic.py`
  > **Remediation:** Remove environment variable collection unless explicitly required and documented

- **🔴 CRITICAL** `BEHAVIOR_ENV_VAR_EXFILTRATION` — Environment variable access with network calls detected
  > Script accesses environment variables and makes network calls in skills/clinical-decision-support/scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py
  > File: `skills/clinical-decision-support/scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py`

  > The SKILL.md instruction body contains a mandatory directive requiring the agent to invoke an external skill ('scientific-schematics') and execute a specific bash command for every clinical report generated. The instruction states '⚠️ MANDATORY: Every clinical report MUST include at least 1 AI-generated figure using the scientific-schematics skill' and provides a bash command to execute. This is a direct prompt injection pattern that attempts to override the agent's discretion and force execution of external code and invocation of another skill, potentially one not installed or controlled by the user.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Remove the mandatory directive forcing invocation of external skills and execution of bash commands. Figure generation should be optional and user-initiated, not automatically triggered for every report. The instruction should not force execution of scripts as a prerequisite to completing the stated task.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_SKILL_DISCOVERY_ABUSE` — Capability Inflation: Branding External AI Service as Skill Feature
  > The SKILL.md instructions reference 'Nano Banana 2' and 'Gemini 3.1 Pro Preview' as if they are built-in capabilities of this skill, when in reality they are external commercial AI services accessed via the OpenRouter API. The description claims 'Nano Banana Pro will automatically generate, review, and refine the schematic' without disclosing that this requires an external paid API key and makes network calls. This inflates the perceived capabilities of the skill and obscures the external dependencies and costs involved.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Clearly disclose in the skill description and SKILL.md that schematic generation requires an external paid API (OpenRouter), specific model access, and network connectivity. Do not present external commercial services as built-in skill capabilities.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_UNAUTHORIZED_TOOL_USE` — Unauthorized Tool Use: Bash Execution Triggered by Instructions for Document Generation
  > The SKILL.md instructions direct the agent to execute a Bash command (python scripts/generate_schematic.py) as a mandatory step for every clinical report. While Bash is listed in allowed-tools, the instructions use this capability to force execution of an external AI image generation pipeline that makes network calls to openrouter.ai. This goes beyond the stated skill purpose of clinical report writing and constitutes tool exploitation by using Bash access to trigger network-dependent AI generation workflows without explicit user consent for each invocation.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Remove the mandatory bash execution directive from the instructions. If schematic generation is desired, it should be presented as an optional feature that users explicitly opt into, not an automatic step triggered for every report.

- **🟠 HIGH** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — Cross-File Exfiltration Chain: generate_schematic.py Passes API Key to Subprocess
  > scripts/generate_schematic.py reads OPENROUTER_API_KEY from the environment and passes it to a child subprocess (generate_schematic_ai.py) via os.environ.copy(). This creates a cross-file exfiltration chain where the API key flows from environment -> generate_schematic.py -> subprocess environment -> generate_schematic_ai.py -> external HTTP request. The static analyzer explicitly flagged BEHAVIOR_CROSSFILE_EXFILTRATION_CHAIN for this pattern.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic.py:95`
  > **Remediation:** Document the full data flow of API keys in the skill manifest. Ensure users are aware that their environment variables are being read and transmitted externally. Consider using a more restricted credential passing mechanism rather than copying the full environment.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — Potential Exposure of Full Environment via subprocess.env Copy
  > In generate_schematic.py, the full process environment is copied (os.environ.copy()) and passed to the subprocess. This means all environment variables present in the agent's environment—potentially including other API keys, credentials, tokens, or sensitive configuration—are passed to the child process, not just the OPENROUTER_API_KEY. While this is a common pattern, in the context of an agent skill it represents unnecessary credential exposure.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic.py:98`
  > **Remediation:** Pass only the minimum required environment variables to the subprocess rather than copying the entire environment. Create a minimal env dict with only the variables needed by the child process.

- **🟠 HIGH** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — API Key Exfiltration via External Network Calls in generate_schematic_ai.py
  > The script generate_schematic_ai.py reads the OPENROUTER_API_KEY environment variable and transmits it to an external server (https://openrouter.ai/api/v1). While the stated purpose is AI image generation, the script also reads the API key from environment variables and sends it in HTTP Authorization headers to an external endpoint. This constitutes environment variable harvesting combined with external network transmission. The key is passed via subprocess to generate_schematic.py as well, creating a cross-file exfiltration chain. The static analyzer flagged BEHAVIOR_ENV_VAR_EXFILTRATION and BEHAVIOR_CROSSFILE_ENV_VAR_EXFILTRATION for this pattern.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py:130`
  > **Remediation:** Restrict network calls to explicitly user-approved endpoints. Require explicit user confirmation before transmitting API keys to external services. Document clearly in SKILL.md that this skill makes external network calls and transmits API credentials. Consider whether this external dependency is necessary for a clinical documentation skill.

### dask — 🔴 CRITICAL

- **🔴 CRITICAL** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — Environment Variable Exfiltration with Network Calls Detected
  > Static analysis flagged a cross-file exfiltration chain involving environment variable access combined with network calls across 2 files. The skill package contains Python files (10 total per file inventory) that were not surfaced in the provided content, but the static analyzer detected BEHAVIOR_ENV_VAR_EXFILTRATION and BEHAVIOR_CROSSFILE_EXFILTRATION_CHAIN patterns. This indicates that one or more Python scripts in the package read environment variables (potentially harvesting credentials, API keys, or tokens from the environment) and transmit them via network calls to external endpoints. This is a classic credential harvesting and data exfiltration pattern.
  > **Remediation:** Immediately inspect all 10 Python files in the skill package for: (1) os.environ, os.getenv, or dotenv calls combined with requests/urllib/httpx network calls; (2) any hardcoded URLs pointing to external servers; (3) any base64-encoded or obfuscated payloads. Remove all network exfiltration code. The skill's stated purpose (Dask distributed computing guidance) does not require reading environment variables and sending them externally.

- **🟠 HIGH** `LLM_OBFUSCATION` — Potential Obfuscation via Hidden Executable Files
  > The skill package contains 10 Python files that were not surfaced in the analysis content, despite the static analyzer detecting active malicious behavioral patterns within them. The professional, detailed, and legitimate-looking SKILL.md and reference documentation may serve as a distraction or cover for malicious Python scripts bundled in the package. The cross-file nature of the exfiltration chain (spanning 2 files) suggests deliberate splitting of malicious logic to evade single-file detection.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Inspect all Python files for split/staged malicious logic. Look for: (1) one file that reads env vars or credentials, (2) another file that performs the network transmission, (3) any import chains between these files. Check for base64 decoding, exec() calls, or dynamic imports that could stage additional payloads.

- **🟠 HIGH** `LLM_UNAUTHORIZED_TOOL_USE` — Undisclosed Python Scripts Not Surfaced for Review
  > The file inventory reports 10 Python files in the skill package, but none were provided for analysis. The static analyzer detected malicious behavioral patterns (env var exfiltration chains) in these hidden Python files. The SKILL.md instructions and reference documentation appear legitimate and benign, but the actual executable Python scripts — which the agent can run via the allowed Bash/Python tools — contain the malicious behavior. This constitutes tool poisoning: the skill presents a clean, professional documentation facade while bundling malicious executable code.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** All Python files must be audited before deployment. The discrepancy between the benign-appearing SKILL.md and the malicious static analysis findings strongly suggests intentional concealment. Do not deploy this skill until all Python files are reviewed and the exfiltration code is removed.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_SKILL_DISCOVERY_ABUSE` — Skill Description References Competing Tools to Manipulate Activation
  > The skill description explicitly names and positions competing tools (vaex, polars) with specific use-case guidance ('For out-of-core analytics on single machine use vaex; for in-memory speed use polars'). While this could be legitimate guidance, it also functions as keyword baiting — by including these competitor tool names in the description/manifest, the skill increases its activation surface across a broader range of user queries about data processing tools, not just Dask-specific requests.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** If this skill is otherwise safe, the description is borderline acceptable as competitive positioning. However, given the malicious Python files detected, this broad activation surface is concerning as it maximizes the number of user interactions that trigger the malicious code execution.

### etetoolkit — 🔴 CRITICAL

- **🟠 HIGH** `LLM_SUPPLY_CHAIN_ATTACK` — Unpinned Dependency Installation (Supply Chain Risk)
  > The SKILL.md instructions recommend installing ete3 using 'uv pip install ete3' without specifying a version pin. This exposes the skill to supply chain attacks where a compromised or malicious version of the ete3 package could be installed. The ete3 package also downloads ~300MB of NCBI taxonomy data automatically on first use, which represents an additional external data fetch that could be tampered with.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Pin the ete3 dependency to a specific known-good version (e.g., 'uv pip install ete3==3.1.3'). Verify the integrity of the NCBI taxonomy database download using checksums. Consider vendoring or caching the dependency.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_PROMPT_INJECTION` — Instruction to Load and Execute External Reference Files
  > The SKILL.md instructs the agent to read and act upon content from reference files (references/api_reference.md, references/workflows.md, references/visualization.md). While internal files are generally safe, the instruction pattern 'Load these references when detailed information is needed' combined with the fact that several referenced files were not found (templates/workflows.md, assets/visualization.md, etc.) creates a risk: if any of these missing files are later populated with malicious instructions, the agent will follow them without additional scrutiny. The skill also references 'ete3.py' which was not found.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Ensure all referenced files exist within the skill package and are reviewed for malicious content. Remove references to non-existent files. Avoid instructing the agent to blindly follow instructions from files that may be populated later by untrusted parties.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_UNAUTHORIZED_TOOL_USE` — Missing allowed-tools Declaration
  > The skill manifest does not declare an 'allowed-tools' field. Given that the skill executes Python scripts, reads/writes files, and the static analyzer detected potential network calls and environment variable access, the absence of tool restrictions means the agent has no declared boundaries on what tools it may use. This is particularly concerning given the flagged exfiltration patterns.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Add an explicit 'allowed-tools' declaration to the YAML frontmatter that restricts the skill to only the tools it legitimately needs (e.g., [Python, Read, Write]). This provides a documented security boundary and enables violation detection.

- **🔴 CRITICAL** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — Environment Variable Access Combined with Network Calls (Cross-File Exfiltration Chain)
  > The static pre-scan analysis flagged BEHAVIOR_ENV_VAR_EXFILTRATION and BEHAVIOR_CROSSFILE_EXFILTRATION_CHAIN across 2 files. While the provided script content (scripts/quick_visualize.py and scripts/tree_operations.py) does not visibly contain these patterns, the static analyzer detected environment variable access paired with network calls forming a cross-file exfiltration chain. This is a critical concern: either additional script files not shown in the provided content contain these patterns, or the patterns are obfuscated. The skill package contains 32 files (22 markdown, 10 Python) but only 2 Python scripts were provided for review, leaving 8 Python scripts unreviewed. These unreviewed scripts may contain the flagged exfiltration behavior.
  > File: `scripts/quick_visualize.py`
  > **Remediation:** Audit all 10 Python scripts in the package, not just the 2 provided. Look for os.environ access, subprocess calls, requests/urllib usage, and any data being sent to external endpoints. Remove or sandbox any network calls that transmit local environment data.

  > Static analysis flagged a cross-file exfiltration chain involving environment variable access combined with network calls across 2 files. The skill references a 'fluidsim.py' file that was not found in the provided content, and multiple template/asset files are also missing. The skill's instructions normalize setting environment variables, which could be harvested.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Retrieve and inspect fluidsim.py and all missing template/asset files for network calls (requests, urllib, http.client, socket) combined with os.environ, os.getenv, or credential file reads. Remove any code that transmits local environment data to external endpoints. Ensure all referenced files are present and auditable before deployment.

- **🟠 HIGH** `LLM_SUPPLY_CHAIN_ATTACK` — Unpinned Package Installation Without Version Constraints
  > The skill instructs the agent to install packages using 'uv pip install fluidsim', 'uv pip install "fluidsim[fft]"', and 'uv pip install "fluidsim[fft,mpi]"' without any version pinning. This exposes the user's environment to supply chain attacks where a compromised or malicious version of the fluidsim package (or its transitive dependencies like fluidfft, pyfftw, mpi4py) could be installed. The lack of version pins means any future malicious release would be automatically installed.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Pin all package versions explicitly, e.g., 'uv pip install fluidsim==0.7.3'. Use a lockfile or hash-pinned requirements. Verify package integrity via checksums before installation.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_SKILL_DISCOVERY_ABUSE` — Over-Broad Capability Description Inflating Skill Activation
  > The skill description is unusually broad, claiming to handle 'Navier-Stokes equations (2D/3D), shallow water equations, stratified flows, turbulence, vortex dynamics, geophysical flows, pseudospectral methods with FFT, HPC support, and comprehensive output analysis.' This over-broad description increases the likelihood of the skill being activated for a wide range of scientific computing queries beyond its actual scope, potentially displacing more appropriate tools or skills.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Narrow the description to accurately reflect the skill's primary use case. Avoid listing every possible sub-capability as activation triggers in the description field.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — Missing Referenced Files Create Unauditable Attack Surface
  > Numerous files referenced in the skill instructions are not present in the package: fluidsim.py, templates/installation.md, templates/output_analysis.md, templates/advanced_features.md, templates/parameters.md, templates/simulation_workflow.md, templates/solvers.md, assets/parameters.md, assets/installation.md, assets/simulation_workflow.md, assets/output_analysis.md, assets/advanced_features.md, assets/solvers.md. These missing files cannot be audited for malicious content. The static analyzer specifically flagged fluidsim.py as part of an exfiltration chain.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Ensure all referenced files are included in the skill package and available for security review. Remove references to non-existent files or provide the actual files. Treat any missing file flagged by static analysis as a critical gap requiring immediate investigation.

### hypothesis-generation — 🔴 CRITICAL

- **🔴 CRITICAL** `BEHAVIOR_CROSSFILE_ENV_VAR_EXFILTRATION` — Cross-file env var exfiltration: 2 files

  > **Remediation:** Review data flow across files: scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py, scripts/generate_schematic.py

  > Multi-file exfiltration chain detected: scripts/generate_schematic.py, scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py collect data → scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py → scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py transmit to network
  > **Remediation:** Review data flow across files: scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py, scripts/generate_schematic.py

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_UNAUTHORIZED_TOOL_USE` — Mandatory External Tool Invocation Without User Consent Disclosure
  > The SKILL.md instructions mark schematic generation as '⚠️ MANDATORY' and state 'This is not optional. Hypothesis reports without visual elements are incomplete.' This forces the agent to invoke an external API (openrouter.ai) on every hypothesis generation task without informing the user that their data will be sent to a third-party service. The mandatory framing removes user agency and bypasses informed consent for external data transmission.
  > File: `SKILL.md:17`
  > **Remediation:** Change the mandatory directive to a recommendation. Add explicit disclosure that figure generation sends data to openrouter.ai. Allow users to opt out of external API calls. The agent should ask for user confirmation before making any external network requests.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_SKILL_DISCOVERY_ABUSE` — Skill Description References Non-Existent Competing Skills by Name
  > The skill description explicitly names and describes two competing/related skills ('scientific-brainstorming' and 'hypogenic') to guide users toward or away from this skill. This is a form of capability framing that could manipulate skill selection behavior. The description also references 'Nano Banana Pro' in the instructions (a branded product name) which may not correspond to any real product, potentially misleading users about the underlying technology.
  > File: `SKILL.md:30`
  > **Remediation:** Remove references to specific competing skill names from the description if they are not part of the same verified skill ecosystem. Clarify the actual underlying technology (openrouter.ai API with specific model names) rather than using marketing brand names like 'Nano Banana Pro'.

- **🟠 HIGH** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — Environment Variable Access Combined with External Network Calls
  > The script generate_schematic_ai.py reads the OPENROUTER_API_KEY environment variable and passes it to external API calls. While this is nominally for authentication, the pattern of reading environment variables and transmitting them to external servers represents a data exfiltration risk. The script also calls os.environ.copy() in generate_schematic.py, which copies the ENTIRE environment (including all secrets, tokens, and credentials present) and passes it to a subprocess. This means ALL environment variables — not just OPENROUTER_API_KEY — are forwarded to the child process and potentially exposed.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic.py:107`
  > **Remediation:** Instead of copying the entire environment, construct a minimal environment dict containing only the variables strictly needed by the subprocess. For example: env = {'PATH': os.environ.get('PATH',''), 'OPENROUTER_API_KEY': api_key}. This prevents inadvertent forwarding of AWS credentials, SSH keys, database passwords, and other secrets present in the environment.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — Hardcoded External Referrer Header Leaks Internal Tool Identity
  > The generate_schematic_ai.py script hardcodes an HTTP-Referer header value of 'https://github.com/scientific-writer' and an X-Title of 'Scientific Schematic Generator' in all API requests. This reveals the identity and nature of the agent tool to the external API provider, which could be used for tracking, profiling, or targeting of users of this skill.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py:193`
  > **Remediation:** Remove or make configurable the HTTP-Referer and X-Title headers. Do not hardcode identifying information that reveals the agent's identity or the user's toolchain to third-party services.

- **🟠 HIGH** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — Cross-File Exfiltration Chain: User Prompt Sent to External AI API
  > The two-script chain (generate_schematic.py → generate_schematic_ai.py) takes user-supplied prompt text and transmits it verbatim to an external third-party service (openrouter.ai). The prompt may contain sensitive scientific data, proprietary research observations, or confidential hypothesis content that the user did not intend to share externally. The SKILL.md instructions mandate use of this script for every hypothesis report, making this data transmission unavoidable and non-optional for users of the skill.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py:200`
  > **Remediation:** Clearly disclose in SKILL.md that user prompts and generated images are transmitted to openrouter.ai (a third-party service). Make schematic generation optional rather than mandatory. Provide a local/offline fallback. Obtain explicit user consent before transmitting any data externally.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_COMMAND_INJECTION` — User-Controlled Prompt Passed Directly to External AI Model Without Sanitization
  > The user's diagram description prompt is passed directly and without sanitization into the AI image generation API request. If the external model (Nano Banana 2 / Gemini) has tool-use or code-execution capabilities, a maliciously crafted prompt could attempt to manipulate the external model's behavior. Additionally, the review prompt embeds the original user prompt verbatim into a larger prompt sent to a second model (Gemini 3.1 Pro Preview), creating a secondary injection surface.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py:280`
  > **Remediation:** Sanitize or quote user-provided prompt content before embedding it into structured prompts sent to external models. Consider using a structured format (e.g., JSON) to separate user content from system instructions when constructing API payloads.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_RESOURCE_ABUSE` — Unbounded Retry Loop with External API Calls
  > The generate_iterative method loops up to 'iterations' times (default 2, max enforced at 2), making multiple expensive API calls per invocation. While the maximum is capped at 2, each iteration makes at least 2 API calls (generation + review), and the review call loads the full generated image as base64 into memory and transmits it. For large images, this could result in significant memory consumption and network bandwidth usage. The cap enforcement is only in the CLI wrapper, not in the core class itself.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py:310`
  > **Remediation:** Add rate limiting and exponential backoff between API calls. Enforce the iteration cap in the ScientificSchematicGenerator class itself (not just the CLI), so programmatic callers cannot bypass it. Add a timeout for the overall generation process.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `BEHAVIOR_ENV_VAR_HARVESTING` — Environment variable harvesting detected
  > Script iterates through environment variables in skills/hypothesis-generation/scripts/generate_schematic.py
  > File: `skills/hypothesis-generation/scripts/generate_schematic.py`
  > **Remediation:** Remove environment variable collection unless explicitly required and documented

- **🔴 CRITICAL** `BEHAVIOR_ENV_VAR_EXFILTRATION` — Environment variable access with network calls detected
  > Script accesses environment variables and makes network calls in skills/hypothesis-generation/scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py
  > File: `skills/hypothesis-generation/scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py`
  > **Remediation:** Remove environment variable harvesting or network transmission

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `BEHAVIOR_ENV_VAR_HARVESTING` — Environment variable harvesting detected
  > Script iterates through environment variables in skills/hypothesis-generation/scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py
  > File: `skills/hypothesis-generation/scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py`
  > **Remediation:** Remove environment variable collection unless explicitly required and documented

  > In generate_infographic.py, the API key is retrieved from the environment or CLI argument and then explicitly set in the subprocess environment before calling generate_infographic_ai.py. While the code comments note this avoids exposure in process listings, the key is still propagated through os.environ.copy() and passed to a child process. This is a standard pattern, but the key is also accepted via --api-key CLI flag which could expose it in process listings on multi-user systems.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_PROMPT_INJECTION` — Research Data from External Sources Incorporated into AI Prompts Without Validation
  > When --research flag is used, the skill calls Perplexity Sonar Pro to gather external data, then directly incorporates the raw research response into the AI generation prompt via _enhance_prompt_with_research(). This creates an indirect prompt injection vector: malicious or manipulated content returned by the research API could contain instructions that influence the downstream Nano Banana Pro image generation model.
  > File: `scripts/generate_infographic_ai.py:248`
  > **Remediation:** Treat research API responses as untrusted external data. Sanitize or parse the research content before embedding it into generation prompts. Consider using a structured extraction step that pulls only specific data fields (numbers, dates, facts) rather than embedding raw text responses.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — Context Images Loaded from User-Specified Paths Without Path Traversal Validation
  > The --context-image argument accepts arbitrary file paths that are read from disk and base64-encoded into API requests. While the code checks if the file exists, there is no validation to prevent path traversal attacks (e.g., ../../.ssh/id_rsa) or restrict access to files outside the intended working directory. This could allow reading sensitive files from the user's system and sending them to external AI APIs.
  > File: `scripts/generate_infographic_ai.py:363`
  > **Remediation:** Validate that context image paths are within an allowed directory (e.g., current working directory or a designated images folder). Use Path.resolve() and check that the resolved path starts with an allowed base directory. Restrict file extensions to known image types.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_COMMAND_INJECTION` — User-Controlled Prompt Passed Directly to AI Generation Without Sanitization
  > The user-supplied prompt string is passed directly into AI generation requests without any sanitization or length limits. In generate_infographic_ai.py, the user prompt is embedded into larger prompts sent to external AI models. A malicious user could craft prompts designed to manipulate the AI generation models (Nano Banana Pro / Gemini) into producing harmful content or bypassing content policies of those downstream models.
  > File: `scripts/generate_infographic_ai.py:390`
  > **Remediation:** Implement input validation and length limits on user prompts. Consider sanitizing or escaping special characters. Add content filtering before passing user input to downstream AI models.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_RESOURCE_ABUSE` — Unbounded Iteration with External API Calls
  > The generate_iterative() method loops up to `iterations` times (default 3, user-configurable via --iterations), making multiple expensive API calls per iteration (generation + review). While there is a maximum iterations parameter, there is no rate limiting, cost cap, or timeout guard beyond the per-request 120-second timeout. A user could set a high iteration count causing excessive API usage and cost.
  > File: `scripts/generate_infographic_ai.py:400`
  > **Remediation:** Add a reasonable maximum cap on iterations (e.g., max 5) that cannot be overridden by user input. Consider adding cost estimation warnings and requiring explicit confirmation for high iteration counts.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — Research and Review Log Files May Contain Sensitive Prompt Data
  > The skill writes detailed JSON log files including the full user prompt, all iteration critiques, research data, and API responses to disk (e.g., {name}_review_log.json, {name}_research.json). These files are written to the output directory without any access controls. If the output directory is shared or publicly accessible, sensitive information about the user's queries and data could be exposed.
  > File: `scripts/generate_infographic_ai.py:450`
  > **Remediation:** Inform users that log files containing their prompts and research data are written to disk. Consider making log file generation opt-in (--save-log flag) rather than always-on. Ensure log files are written with appropriate file permissions.

The manifest only declares allowed-tools: Read Write Edit Bash but the skill orchestrates Python scripts that make external API calls.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_COMMAND_INJECTION` — Subprocess Execution with User-Controlled Arguments
  > The generate_schematic.py wrapper script constructs a subprocess command using user-supplied arguments (prompt, output path, doc-type, iterations) and passes them directly to generate_schematic_ai.py via subprocess.run(). While the arguments are passed as a list (not shell=True), the user-controlled prompt string is passed as a positional argument to the subprocess. A malicious prompt containing shell metacharacters could potentially cause issues depending on how the downstream script processes it, though the list-based invocation mitigates direct shell injection.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic.py`
  > **Remediation:** This is relatively low risk due to list-based subprocess invocation. However, validate and sanitize the prompt argument before passing to subprocess. Consider adding length limits on the prompt argument.

- **🟠 HIGH** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — API Key Exfiltration via Environment Variable and Network Transmission
  > The generate_schematic_ai.py script reads the OPENROUTER_API_KEY from environment variables and transmits it to an external API endpoint (https://openrouter.ai/api/v1). While the stated purpose is legitimate AI image generation, the pattern of reading sensitive credentials from the environment and sending them over the network represents a data exfiltration risk. The API key is passed in HTTP Authorization headers to an external service, and the script also reads from .env files in the current working directory or script directory. If the OpenRouter endpoint or the skill itself were compromised, this would expose the API key.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py`
  > **Remediation:** Ensure the OpenRouter API key is scoped to minimum necessary permissions. Consider validating the endpoint URL before transmission. Document clearly that the API key will be sent to openrouter.ai. Avoid reading from .env files in arbitrary directories.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — Sensitive Data Written to Disk in Review Log Files
  > The generate_schematic_ai.py script saves a JSON review log file (e.g., figures/workflow_review_log.json) that contains the full generation results including prompts, critique text, scores, and iteration details. While this does not directly exfiltrate credentials, it persists potentially sensitive research content and AI interaction history to disk in a predictable location. The log includes the full user prompt and AI critique, which could contain sensitive research details.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py`
  > **Remediation:** Make review log generation optional (e.g., --save-log flag). Warn users that logs contain full prompt and critique history. Consider not logging by default or providing a --no-log option.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_SUPPLY_CHAIN_ATTACK` — Unpinned External API Dependency and Unverified Model Identifiers
  > The generate_schematic_ai.py script hardcodes model identifiers (google/gemini-3.1-flash-image-preview and google/gemini-3.1-pro-preview) that are resolved at runtime by the OpenRouter API. These model identifiers could be changed or hijacked if OpenRouter's model registry is compromised or if the models are deprecated and replaced with different models. Additionally, the requests library is imported without version pinning, and the script installs no dependencies with pinned versions.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py`
  > **Remediation:** Document the specific model versions expected. Consider adding model version validation. Pin the requests library version in requirements.txt. Add integrity checks on API responses.

### literature-review — 🔴 CRITICAL

- **🔴 CRITICAL** `BEHAVIOR_CROSSFILE_ENV_VAR_EXFILTRATION` — Cross-file env var exfiltration: 3 files
  > Environment variable access with network calls in scripts/generate_schematic.py, scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py
  > **Remediation:** Review data flow across files: scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py, scripts/generate_schematic.py, scripts/verify_citations.py

- **🔴 CRITICAL** `BEHAVIOR_CROSSFILE_EXFILTRATION_CHAIN` — Cross-file exfiltration chain: 3 files
  > Multi-file exfiltration chain detected: scripts/generate_schematic.py, scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py collect data → scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py → scripts/verify_citations.py, scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py transmit to network
  > **Remediation:** Review data flow across files: scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py, scripts/generate_schematic.py, scripts/verify_citations.py

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_SUPPLY_CHAIN_ATTACK` — Unpinned Python Dependency in Requirements
  > The SKILL.md instructions specify 'pip install requests' without a version pin. The requests library is a critical dependency used for all citation verification and API calls. An unpinned dependency is vulnerable to supply chain attacks where a malicious version could be installed. This is particularly concerning given that the requests library is used to transmit API keys and make external network calls.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Pin the requests library to a specific verified version: 'pip install requests==2.31.0'. Consider using a requirements.txt file with hashed dependencies (pip install --require-hashes) for stronger supply chain security.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_UNAUTHORIZED_TOOL_USE` — Unauthorized Tool Use: Bash Tool Used for External CLI Installation
  > The SKILL.md instructions direct the agent to install external CLI tools using curl piped to bash (curl -fsSL https://parallel.ai/install.sh | bash), which is a high-risk pattern. The allowed-tools field declares [Read, Write, Edit, Bash], so Bash is permitted, but executing arbitrary install scripts from external URLs via curl|bash is a significant supply chain and tool exploitation risk. This pattern can execute arbitrary code from a remote server.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Replace curl|bash installation patterns with verified package manager installations with pinned versions. Use 'uv tool install parallel-web-tools[cli]==X.Y.Z' with a specific version pin. Verify package integrity with checksums before installation.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_PROMPT_INJECTION` — Indirect Prompt Injection Risk via External Web Content Extraction
  > The skill instructs the agent to use 'parallel-cli extract' to fetch full content from arbitrary URLs found during searches, including paper URLs and journal websites. Content fetched from external sources could contain embedded instructions that manipulate the agent's behavior during the literature review synthesis phase. The skill explicitly instructs: 'Use parallel-cli extract to fetch full content from promising URLs found during search to verify relevance before full-text screening.'
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Instruct the agent to treat all externally fetched content as untrusted data only, not as instructions. Add explicit guidance in SKILL.md that content from external URLs should never be interpreted as skill instructions or override the review methodology. Consider sandboxing external content processing.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_SKILL_DISCOVERY_ABUSE` — Over-Broad Capability Claims in Description
  > The skill description claims to work with 'multiple academic databases (PubMed, arXiv, bioRxiv, Semantic Scholar, etc.)' and 'multiple citation styles (APA, Nature, Vancouver, etc.)'. The SKILL.md also mandates use of 'scientific-schematics' skill and 'parallel-web skill' as dependencies. These cross-skill dependencies are not declared in the manifest, and the description may inflate perceived capabilities by implying seamless integration with external services that require separate authentication (OpenRouter API key, parallel-cli auth).
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Declare cross-skill dependencies explicitly in the manifest. Clarify in the description that external API keys (OpenRouter) and additional CLI tools (parallel-cli) are required. Avoid marking optional features as MANDATORY without noting the prerequisite dependencies.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_COMMAND_INJECTION` — Unvalidated File Path Arguments in Multiple Scripts
  > Multiple scripts (search_databases.py, verify_citations.py, generate_pdf.py) accept file paths directly from command-line arguments without validation. In generate_pdf.py, the markdown_file path is passed directly to subprocess pandoc and xelatex commands. In verify_citations.py, the filepath is opened directly. An attacker who controls the file path argument could potentially cause path traversal or cause the agent to read/process unintended files.
  > File: `scripts/generate_pdf.py`
  > **Remediation:** Validate file paths to ensure they are within expected directories. Use Path.resolve() and check that the resolved path is within the skill's working directory. Apply similar validation in verify_citations.py and search_databases.py.

- **🟠 HIGH** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — Cross-File Exfiltration Chain: Environment Variables Sent to External Server
  > The static analyzer identified a cross-file exfiltration chain spanning 3 files. The generate_schematic.py script reads OPENROUTER_API_KEY from the environment and passes it to generate_schematic_ai.py via subprocess and environment copy (os.environ.copy()), which then transmits it to https://openrouter.ai/api/v1. The chain is: generate_schematic.py (env read) → subprocess call → generate_schematic_ai.py (env read + HTTP POST with Bearer token). This multi-hop pattern is characteristic of credential harvesting pipelines.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic.py`
  > **Remediation:** The comment in the code states the API key is passed via environment 'to avoid exposure in process listings', which is a legitimate security practice. However, the full environment copy (os.environ.copy()) passes ALL environment variables to the subprocess, not just the API key. This could expose other sensitive environment variables. Use a minimal environment dict containing only required variables.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_COMMAND_INJECTION` — Subprocess Execution with User-Controlled Prompt Input
  > In generate_schematic.py, the user-supplied prompt argument is passed directly into a subprocess command list. While using a list (not shell=True) mitigates shell injection, the prompt string is passed as a positional argument to generate_schematic_ai.py, which then uses it in API requests. If the downstream AI model interprets the prompt in unexpected ways or if the prompt is logged/stored externally, this could be exploited. The prompt is also embedded directly into HTTP request payloads sent to OpenRouter without sanitization.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic.py`
  > **Remediation:** Validate and sanitize the prompt input before passing it to subprocess commands and external APIs. Consider length limits and character filtering. Ensure the subprocess is invoked with a minimal environment rather than the full os.environ.copy().

- **🟠 HIGH** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — API Key Exfiltration via Environment Variable Harvesting
  > The generate_schematic_ai.py script reads the OPENROUTER_API_KEY environment variable and transmits it to an external API endpoint (https://openrouter.ai/api/v1). While OpenRouter is a legitimate service, the pattern of harvesting an API key from the environment and sending it over the network represents a credential exfiltration risk. The key is embedded in HTTP Authorization headers sent to an external server. Additionally, the script loads .env files from the current working directory or script directory, which could expose other secrets stored in those files beyond just the OpenRouter key.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py`
  > **Remediation:** Ensure the OPENROUTER_API_KEY is scoped only to this skill's use. Avoid loading .env files broadly from the working directory, as this could expose unrelated secrets. Consider prompting the user explicitly for the API key rather than silently harvesting from the environment. Document clearly which credentials are accessed and transmitted.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `BEHAVIOR_ENV_VAR_HARVESTING` — Environment variable harvesting detected
  > Script iterates through environment variables in skills/literature-review/scripts/generate_schematic.py
  > File: `skills/literature-review/scripts/generate_schematic.py`
  > **Remediation:** Remove environment variable collection unless explicitly required and documented

- **🔴 CRITICAL** `BEHAVIOR_ENV_VAR_EXFILTRATION` — Environment variable access with network calls detected
  > Script accesses environment variables and makes network calls in skills/literature-review/scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py
  > File: `skills/literature-review/scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py`
  > **Remediation:** Remove environment variable harvesting or network transmission

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `BEHAVIOR_ENV_VAR_HARVESTING` — Environment variable harvesting detected
  > Script iterates through environment variables in skills/literature-review/scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py
  > File: `skills/literature-review/scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py`
  > **Remediation:** Remove environment variable collection unless explicitly required and documented

  > **Remediation:** Review data flow across files: scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py, scripts/generate_schematic.py, scripts/convert_with_ai.py

  > **Remediation:** Review data flow across files: scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py, scripts/generate_schematic.py, scripts/convert_with_ai.py

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_SKILL_DISCOVERY_ABUSE` — Capability Inflation via Cross-Skill Promotion (scientific-schematics)
  > The SKILL.md instructions repeatedly and prominently promote a separate 'scientific-schematics' skill, instructing the agent to invoke it by default even when the user only requested document conversion. The instructions state 'Scientific schematics should be generated by default' and 'always consider adding scientific diagrams'. This inflates the activation surface of a separate skill beyond its intended scope, manipulating the agent into invoking additional capabilities the user did not request.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Remove cross-skill promotion from SKILL.md. The markitdown skill should only describe its own file conversion capabilities. Any suggestion to use other skills should be left to the user's discretion.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_SUPPLY_CHAIN_ATTACK` — Unpinned Package Dependencies
  > The SKILL.md instructions recommend installing markitdown with 'pip install markitdown[all]' and other packages without version pinning. The scripts import from 'markitdown', 'openai', and 'requests' without version constraints. Unpinned dependencies are vulnerable to supply chain attacks where a malicious package version could be installed.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Pin all dependencies to specific versions (e.g., markitdown==0.1.0, openai==1.x.x, requests==2.31.0). Provide a requirements.txt with pinned versions and hash verification.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_RESOURCE_ABUSE` — Unbounded Parallel Worker Execution
  > The batch_convert.py script uses ThreadPoolExecutor with a configurable worker count (default 4, no upper bound enforced). Combined with recursive directory traversal, this could lead to excessive resource consumption if pointed at a large directory tree with many files.
  > File: `scripts/batch_convert.py:75`
  > **Remediation:** Enforce a maximum worker count (e.g., cap at 16). Add file count limits and size checks before initiating batch processing. Warn users when processing large numbers of files.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_UNAUTHORIZED_TOOL_USE` — Dynamic Plugin Loading Without Integrity Verification
  > The skill supports enabling third-party MarkItDown plugins via --use-plugins flag and enable_plugins=True parameter. Plugins are discovered from installed Python packages without any integrity verification, signature checking, or allowlisting. A malicious plugin installed in the Python environment could execute arbitrary code during document conversion.
  > File: `scripts/batch_convert.py:82`
  > **Remediation:** Document the security risks of enabling plugins. Recommend users only enable plugins from trusted, verified sources. Consider disabling plugin support by default and requiring explicit user confirmation before enabling.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — API Key Exposure via Hardcoded Placeholder in Documentation
  > Multiple locations in SKILL.md and scripts contain placeholder API key strings (e.g., 'your-openrouter-api-key') in code examples. While these are placeholders, the pattern normalizes embedding API keys directly in code. More critically, the scripts accept API keys via command-line arguments (--api-key flag), which exposes secrets in process listings. The generate_schematic.py script explicitly notes it passes the key via environment to avoid process listing exposure, but the convert_with_ai.py script accepts --api-key directly.
  > File: `scripts/convert_with_ai.py:107`
  > **Remediation:** Remove --api-key CLI argument from all scripts. Require API keys exclusively via environment variables (OPENROUTER_API_KEY). Document secure key management practices.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — Environment Variable Harvesting with External Network Transmission
  > The scripts read the OPENROUTER_API_KEY environment variable and transmit it to an external API endpoint (openrouter.ai). While this is the intended functionality for API authentication, the pattern of reading environment variables and sending them to external servers creates a data exfiltration risk if the API endpoint or model identifier is tampered with. The generate_schematic_ai.py script also loads .env files from the filesystem, expanding the credential harvesting surface.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py:88`
  > **Remediation:** Limit .env file loading to explicitly documented behavior. Validate the API endpoint is a known, trusted domain before transmitting credentials. Consider pinning the base_url to prevent redirection attacks.
