### pacsomatic — 🔴 CRITICAL

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_SKILL_DISCOVERY_ABUSE` — Missing allowed-tools and compatibility Metadata
  > The SKILL.md manifest does not specify allowed-tools or compatibility fields. While these are optional per the spec, their absence means there are no declared constraints on what tools the agent may use when executing this skill. The skill executes subprocess calls, writes files, and potentially clones git repositories, which are significant capabilities that benefit from explicit declaration.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Add allowed-tools to the YAML frontmatter listing the tools actually used (e.g., Bash, Python). Add compatibility information describing supported platforms. This improves transparency and allows downstream security tooling to detect violations.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_SUPPLY_CHAIN_ATTACK` — Unpinned Pipeline Version and Remote Repository Cloning
  > The skill defaults to cloning from https://github.com/nf-core/pacsomatic.git without pinning a specific commit or tag. The --pipeline-version flag is optional and defaults to empty, meaning the latest HEAD is used. This creates a supply chain risk where a compromised or updated upstream repository could alter pipeline behavior without the user's knowledge.
  > File: `scripts/run_pacsomatic.py:113`
  > **Remediation:** Recommend or enforce use of --pipeline-version with a pinned release tag or commit hash. Document this as a best practice in SKILL.md (it is mentioned in references/pacsomatic_guide.md but not enforced). Consider warning when --pipeline-version is not set in --run mode.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — Sensitive Path Information Written to Samplesheet and Params Files
  > The generated samplesheet CSV and params YAML contain full absolute paths to BAM files, reference FASTA, and output directories. These files are written to disk and their paths are printed to stdout. While this is expected behavior for a bioinformatics workflow tool, the agent should be aware that these artifacts may expose sensitive filesystem layout information if shared or logged.
  > File: `scripts/run_pacsomatic.py:196`
  > **Remediation:** Informational only. Ensure generated artifacts are written to appropriately permissioned directories. Consider documenting that samplesheet and params files contain sensitive path information and should not be shared publicly.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_COMMAND_INJECTION` — Unsanitized --extra-args Passed Directly to Nextflow Command
  > The --extra-args argument is split using shlex.split() and appended directly to the Nextflow command. While shlex.split() handles quoting, it does not prevent injection of arbitrary Nextflow flags or parameters. A malicious or careless user could inject flags like --config /etc/passwd or other Nextflow options that alter pipeline behavior in unintended ways. This is particularly relevant since the agent may construct this argument from user-provided natural language input.
  > File: `scripts/run_pacsomatic.py:248`
  > **Remediation:** Consider removing --extra-args or restricting it to a whitelist of known safe Nextflow flags. At minimum, document clearly that this argument accepts raw shell tokens and should not be populated from untrusted user input without validation.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_COMMAND_INJECTION` — --module-load Argument Written Verbatim into Shell Script
  > The --module-load argument is written directly into the generated bash launch script without any sanitization or escaping. If a user or agent provides a malicious value (e.g., containing semicolons, newlines, or subshell syntax), it would be executed as arbitrary shell code when the script runs. The script uses set -euo pipefail but this does not prevent injection via the module load line itself.
  > File: `scripts/run_pacsomatic.py:295`
  > **Remediation:** Validate --module-load against a strict allowlist pattern (e.g., only allow 'module load <name>/<version>' format). Alternatively, use shlex.quote() on the argument or split it into safe components before embedding in the script.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_COMMAND_INJECTION` — Shell Injection via shell=True with User-Controlled Script Path
  > The execute_launch() function calls subprocess.run() with shell=True and a command string constructed from user-controlled input (the script_path argument, which derives from --script-path or default_script_path). While shlex.quote() is applied to the script path, using shell=True with a constructed string still introduces risk if any other part of the command string is ever modified or if the executor value is attacker-controlled. The executor value is constrained by argparse choices, but the overall pattern of shell=True with a dynamically constructed command string is a code quality/security concern.
  > File: `scripts/run_pacsomatic.py:310`
  > **Remediation:** Refactor execute_launch() to use a list-based subprocess call (shell=False) instead of shell=True. For example, parse the command string back into a list using shlex.split() or construct the list directly in submit_command_for_executor(). This eliminates shell interpretation entirely.

- **🔴 CRITICAL** `BEHAVIOR_EVAL_SUBPROCESS` — eval/exec combined with subprocess detected
  > Dangerous combination of code execution and system commands in skills/pacsomatic/scripts/run_pacsomatic.py
  > File: `skills/pacsomatic/scripts/run_pacsomatic.py`
  > **Remediation:** Remove eval/exec or use safer alternatives

### peer-review — 🔴 CRITICAL

  > **Remediation:** Review data flow across files: scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py, scripts/generate_schematic.py

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_UNAUTHORIZED_TOOL_USE` — Unauthorized Tool Use: Bash and Python Execution Not Declared in allowed-tools
  > The SKILL.md manifest declares allowed-tools as 'Read Write Edit Bash', but the skill instructions explicitly direct the agent to execute Python scripts (python scripts/generate_schematic.py ...) and the scripts themselves use subprocess.run() to spawn child Python processes. The 'Python' tool is not listed in allowed-tools, yet Python execution is a core part of the skill's workflow. Additionally, the instructions direct the agent to run pdf_to_images.py from a different skill (scientific-slides), which is cross-skill tool invocation not declared in the manifest.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Add 'Python' to the allowed-tools list if Python execution is intended. Remove or clearly document the cross-skill dependency on scientific-slides. Ensure the manifest accurately reflects all tools and capabilities used by the skill.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_SKILL_DISCOVERY_ABUSE` — Cross-Skill Capability Inflation: References Non-Existent 'scientific-schematics' Skill
  > The SKILL.md instructions prominently advertise integration with a 'scientific-schematics' skill and 'Nano Banana Pro' product, directing the agent to use these for diagram generation. The instructions state 'Nano Banana Pro will automatically generate, review, and refine the schematic' and reference 'scientific-schematics skill documentation'. These references inflate the perceived capabilities of this skill by implying integration with external products/skills that may not exist or be installed, potentially causing the agent to attempt to invoke non-existent skills.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Remove references to external skills or products that are not bundled with this skill package. If cross-skill dependencies exist, document them explicitly in the manifest metadata rather than embedding them as implicit instructions. Verify that referenced skills are available before directing the agent to use them.

- **🟠 HIGH** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — Cross-File Exfiltration Chain: Environment Variable Harvesting Across Two Scripts
  > The static analyzer identified a cross-file exfiltration chain spanning generate_schematic.py and generate_schematic_ai.py. generate_schematic.py reads OPENROUTER_API_KEY from the environment (os.getenv), copies the entire environment (os.environ.copy()), and passes it to generate_schematic_ai.py via subprocess. generate_schematic_ai.py then uses this key in outbound HTTP requests. Passing the full os.environ.copy() to the subprocess means ALL environment variables (not just OPENROUTER_API_KEY) are forwarded to the child process, which could include AWS credentials, SSH keys, tokens, and other secrets present in the environment.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic.py:108`
  > **Remediation:** Instead of passing os.environ.copy() (which forwards ALL environment variables), construct a minimal environment containing only the variables needed by the child process. Example: env = {"OPENROUTER_API_KEY": api_key, "PATH": os.environ.get("PATH", "")}. This prevents inadvertent forwarding of sensitive credentials like AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY, GITHUB_TOKEN, etc.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — API Key Potentially Exposed in .env File Loading from Current Working Directory
  > The generate_schematic_ai.py script attempts to load a .env file from the current working directory (Path.cwd() / '.env') using python-dotenv. This means if the agent is run from a directory containing a .env file with sensitive credentials, those credentials will be loaded into the environment and potentially used or forwarded. The script loads from cwd without user awareness, which could inadvertently expose credentials from unrelated projects.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py:35`
  > **Remediation:** Limit .env file loading to the skill's own directory only (not cwd). Document clearly that a .env file will be loaded if present. Consider requiring explicit opt-in for .env file loading rather than automatic discovery.

- **🟠 HIGH** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — API Key Exfiltration via External Network Calls with User-Controlled Prompt
  > The scripts generate_schematic.py and generate_schematic_ai.py read the OPENROUTER_API_KEY from environment variables and transmit it in HTTP Authorization headers to an external API (openrouter.ai). While the stated purpose is AI image generation, the user-controlled 'prompt' argument is passed directly into API requests, and the API key is sent to an external server. The cross-file chain (generate_schematic.py → generate_schematic_ai.py) passes the API key via environment variable, and both scripts make outbound network calls with this credential. This constitutes credential exposure to an external third-party service.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py:130`
  > **Remediation:** Ensure the API key is only used for its stated purpose and not logged or transmitted elsewhere. Validate that openrouter.ai is the intended and trusted endpoint. Consider scoping API key permissions. Warn users explicitly that their OPENROUTER_API_KEY will be transmitted to openrouter.ai before invoking the script.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_COMMAND_INJECTION` — User-Controlled Prompt Passed Unsanitized to External AI API
  > The user-supplied 'prompt' argument from the command line is passed directly and without sanitization into the API request payload sent to openrouter.ai. While this is a generation API rather than a code execution context, the prompt is also used to construct subsequent 'improved' prompts via improve_prompt(), which incorporates AI-generated critique text. This creates a chain where external AI-generated content (the critique) is concatenated into subsequent prompts without validation, enabling potential prompt injection through the review model's output influencing the generation model's input.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py:310`
  > **Remediation:** Sanitize or validate the critique text returned from the review model before incorporating it into subsequent generation prompts. Consider using structured output formats for the review response rather than free-form text concatenation. Limit the length and content of critique text that can be injected into subsequent prompts.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_PROMPT_INJECTION` — Indirect Prompt Injection via AI-Generated Critique Incorporated into Agent Instructions
  > The generate_schematic_ai.py script retrieves free-form text from an external AI model (Gemini 3.1 Pro Preview via openrouter.ai) as a 'critique', then incorporates this externally-sourced text directly into subsequent prompts sent to another AI model. If the review model returns malicious or manipulative content in its critique, that content is injected verbatim into the next generation prompt. This is an indirect prompt injection vector where external AI-generated content can influence subsequent AI behavior without sanitization.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py:310`
  > **Remediation:** Treat AI-generated critique text as untrusted external input. Parse structured fields (score, verdict) separately from free-form critique text. Do not concatenate raw AI-generated text into subsequent prompts without validation. Use structured output schemas for the review model response.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `BEHAVIOR_ENV_VAR_HARVESTING` — Environment variable harvesting detected
  > Script iterates through environment variables in skills/peer-review/scripts/generate_schematic.py
  > File: `skills/peer-review/scripts/generate_schematic.py`
  > **Remediation:** Remove environment variable collection unless explicitly required and documented

  > Script accesses environment variables and makes network calls in skills/peer-review/scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py
  > File: `skills/peer-review/scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py`
  > **Remediation:** Remove environment variable harvesting or network transmission

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_SKILL_DISCOVERY_ABUSE` — Skill Activation Guidance May Cause Unintended Invocation
  > The SKILL.md contains extensive guidance directing the agent to use 'latex-posters' skill for most poster requests, and to use this skill ONLY for explicit PPTX requests. However, the description field in the YAML manifest mentions 'research posters' broadly, which could cause the skill to be activated by general poster queries before the agent reads the detailed instructions. The description could be more restrictive to match the narrow activation criteria defined in the instructions.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Make the YAML description more restrictive and specific (e.g., 'Create PPTX/PowerPoint format research posters only - for standard posters use latex-posters skill') to reduce unintended activation by general poster queries.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_COMMAND_INJECTION` — Subprocess Execution with User-Controlled Arguments
  > The wrapper script (generate_schematic.py) constructs a subprocess command using user-provided arguments (prompt, output path, doc-type, iterations) and passes them directly to generate_schematic_ai.py via subprocess.run(). While the arguments are passed as a list (not shell=True), the output path and prompt are user-controlled and passed without validation, which could lead to path traversal or argument injection issues depending on how the downstream script handles them.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic.py`
  > **Remediation:** Validate and sanitize the output path to prevent path traversal (e.g., ensure it stays within the working directory). Validate the prompt does not contain shell metacharacters even though shell=False is used. Consider using absolute paths and restricting output locations.

- **🟠 HIGH** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — API Key Harvesting via Environment Variable and Network Transmission
  > The scripts read the OPENROUTER_API_KEY environment variable and transmit it as a Bearer token in HTTP requests to openrouter.ai. While the stated purpose is AI image generation, the pattern of reading sensitive credentials from the environment and sending them over the network represents a credential exposure risk. The API key is passed through subprocess calls and environment copies, creating multiple points where it could be intercepted or logged. Additionally, the script accepts --api-key as a CLI argument, which would expose the key in process listings (though the wrapper script does attempt to pass it via environment instead).
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py`
  > **Remediation:** Ensure the skill clearly discloses to users that their OPENROUTER_API_KEY will be transmitted to openrouter.ai. Validate the destination URL is strictly openrouter.ai before sending credentials. Remove the --api-key CLI flag to prevent key exposure in process listings. Consider using a secrets manager or keyring instead of environment variables.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — User-Controlled Prompt Content Sent to External AI API
  > The user's prompt (diagram description) is passed directly to an external API (openrouter.ai) without sanitization or disclosure. Any content the user provides — including potentially sensitive research data, proprietary information, or confidential details — is transmitted to a third-party service. The skill does not warn users that their input will be sent externally. The cross-file chain (generate_schematic.py → generate_schematic_ai.py) means user input flows from the wrapper to the AI backend transparently.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py`
  > **Remediation:** Add explicit disclosure in SKILL.md that user prompts and poster content will be transmitted to openrouter.ai (a third-party service). Allow users to opt out or confirm before sending data externally. Document data handling and privacy implications clearly.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_PROMPT_INJECTION` — User-Provided Prompt Content Injected into AI Model Requests Without Sanitization
  > The user's natural language prompt describing the diagram is embedded directly into structured AI model requests sent to external APIs. The prompt is also augmented with SCIENTIFIC_DIAGRAM_GUIDELINES and review prompts that include the original user prompt verbatim. A malicious user could craft a prompt containing instruction-injection payloads targeting the downstream AI models (Gemini 3.1 Pro Preview, Nano Banana 2), potentially manipulating the quality review scores or causing the review model to produce unexpected outputs that are then logged and processed.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py`
  > **Remediation:** Sanitize or delimit user-provided prompt content before embedding it in structured AI requests. Consider wrapping user input in clear delimiters and instructing the model to treat it as data, not instructions. Validate that extracted scores and verdicts conform to expected formats before acting on them.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_SUPPLY_CHAIN_ATTACK` — Unpinned External Dependency (requests library)
  > The script imports the 'requests' library without a pinned version requirement. The error message suggests installing via 'pip install requests' without specifying a version. Unpinned dependencies are vulnerable to supply chain attacks where a compromised or malicious version could be installed.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py`
  > **Remediation:** Pin the requests library to a specific known-good version (e.g., requests==2.31.0) in a requirements.txt file. Use a lockfile or hash verification to ensure dependency integrity.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_SKILL_DISCOVERY_ABUSE` — Skill References Non-Existent 'scientific-schematics' Companion Skill
  > The SKILL.md instructions reference a 'scientific-schematics' skill as a complementary tool and instruct the agent to 'always consider adding scientific diagrams' using it. This creates an implicit dependency on an external skill that may not be installed, and the instruction to 'always' use it could cause the agent to attempt to invoke a non-existent skill or generate unexpected behavior. The generate_schematic.py script is bundled locally, but the SKILL.md references it as if it were a separate skill.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Clarify in the instructions that the schematic generation is handled by the bundled scripts/generate_schematic.py rather than a separate skill. Remove or qualify the reference to 'scientific-schematics' skill to avoid agent confusion about available capabilities.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_SUPPLY_CHAIN_ATTACK` — Unpinned External Tool Installation via curl Pipe to Bash
  > The SKILL.md instructions recommend installing parallel-cli via 'curl -fsSL https://parallel.ai/install.sh | bash' without any integrity verification (no checksum, no signature verification). This is a supply chain risk — if the install.sh script at parallel.ai is compromised or the domain is hijacked, arbitrary code could be executed on the user's machine. An alternative 'uv tool install' method is also provided without version pinning.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Provide a pinned version for the uv install command (e.g., 'uv tool install parallel-web-tools[cli]==X.Y.Z'). Document the expected checksum or signature for the install script. Prefer the package manager approach over curl-pipe-bash. Add a note warning users to verify the installation source.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — User Query Text Transmitted to External APIs Without Explicit Consent Mechanism
  > The skill transmits user research queries directly to external third-party APIs (api.parallel.ai via PARALLEL_API_KEY and openrouter.ai via OPENROUTER_API_KEY). While this is disclosed in the SKILL.md description, the actual query content — which may contain sensitive research topics, proprietary information, or confidential data — is sent to these external services. The skill does not implement any sanitization, filtering, or user confirmation before transmitting query content externally. This is partially mitigated by the upfront disclosure in the manifest description.
  > File: `research_lookup.py`
  > **Remediation:** Add explicit user confirmation before transmitting queries to external APIs, especially for sensitive research topics. Consider adding a data classification check or warning when queries may contain proprietary information. Document data retention policies for both api.parallel.ai and openrouter.ai.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — API Keys Read from Environment Variables and Transmitted in HTTP Headers
  > The skill reads PARALLEL_API_KEY and OPENROUTER_API_KEY from environment variables and uses them in HTTP Authorization headers. While this is standard practice, the keys are passed directly into requests without any validation, masking in logs, or rotation support. The generate_schematic.py script also passes the API key via environment to subprocess calls, which is the correct approach, but the key is still present in the process environment.
  > File: `research_lookup.py`
  > **Remediation:** Validate that API keys are non-empty and match expected format before use. Avoid logging API keys. Consider using a secrets manager rather than raw environment variables. The HTTP-Referer header 'https://scientific-writer.local' is a non-existent domain used as an identifier — document this clearly to avoid confusion.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — Research Results Saved to Local Filesystem Without Path Validation
  > The skill mandates saving all research results to a 'sources/' folder using the -o flag. The output file path is constructed using user-provided topic strings (e.g., 'sources/research_<topic>.json'). While the topic is used in filenames rather than executed, there is no validation or sanitization of the topic string used in file paths, which could lead to path traversal if a malicious topic string like '../../../etc/passwd' is used as a filename component.
  > File: `research_lookup.py`
  > **Remediation:** Sanitize output file paths to prevent path traversal. Use os.path.basename() on user-provided filename components, or validate that the resolved path stays within the intended 'sources/' directory using os.path.realpath() and checking the prefix.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_RESOURCE_ABUSE` — Batch Query Processing Without Rate Limiting or Resource Bounds
  > The batch_lookup() method accepts an unbounded list of queries and processes them sequentially with only a configurable delay between requests. There is no maximum batch size limit, no total timeout, and no circuit breaker. A large batch could exhaust API rate limits, incur significant costs, or cause extended blocking of the agent. The default delay of 1.0 second is minimal protection.
  > File: `research_lookup.py`
  > **Remediation:** Add a maximum batch size limit (e.g., 20 queries). Implement a total timeout for batch operations. Add cost estimation before executing large batches. Consider adding a user confirmation prompt for batches exceeding a threshold size.

  > The SKILL.md instructions contain a prominent section that instructs the agent to automatically invoke a separate 'scientific-schematics' skill and run generate_schematic.py by default for any document created with this skill, even when the user has not requested diagrams. The instruction states 'Scientific schematics should be generated by default' and 'always consider adding scientific diagrams.' This is a form of capability inflation / cross-skill activation abuse that causes the agent to invoke additional tools and skills beyond the user's stated request, potentially triggering additional API calls and resource consumption without explicit user consent.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** 1. Change the instruction from 'by default' and 'always' to 'when explicitly requested by the user.' 2. - **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — Cross-File Exfiltration Chain: generate_schematic.py Delegates to generate_schematic_ai.py
  > The generate_schematic.py script acts as a launcher that invokes generate_schematic_ai.py via subprocess, passing the API key through the environment. This two-file chain means the full credential and network call behavior is split across files, making it harder to audit. The parent script (generate_schematic.py) explicitly copies os.environ and injects the API key before spawning the child process. This pattern is consistent with a credential-passing exfiltration chain flagged by static analysis.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic.py`
  > **Remediation:** 1. Consolidate the two scripts into one to improve auditability. 2. Document the subprocess invocation pattern clearly. 3. Avoid copying the entire os.environ (which may contain unrelated secrets) — pass only the specific required variables.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — Environment Variable Access Combined with External Network Calls
  > The generate_schematic_ai.py script reads the OPENROUTER_API_KEY environment variable and uses it to make outbound HTTP requests to openrouter.ai. While the stated purpose is AI image generation, the combination of environment variable harvesting and network calls represents a data flow that could expose API keys or other environment variables to an external service. The API key is passed in Authorization headers to an external third-party service (openrouter.ai), and the script also reads from .env files on disk. If the API key or .env file contains sensitive credentials beyond just the OpenRouter key, this could result in unintended credential exposure.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py`
  > **Remediation:** 1. Clearly document in SKILL.md that this skill makes outbound network calls to openrouter.ai and requires an API key. 2. Scope the .env file loading to only the specific key needed. 3. Avoid loading .env files from the current working directory (cwd), as this could pick up unrelated project secrets. 4. Add user confirmation before making external API calls with credentials.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_RESOURCE_ABUSE` — Unbounded External API Calls with Iterative Refinement Loop
  > The generate_schematic_ai.py script implements an iterative refinement loop that makes multiple calls to external AI APIs (image generation + quality review per iteration). While the maximum iterations are capped at 2, each iteration makes at least 2 API calls (one to gemini-3.1-flash-image-preview for generation, one to gemini-3.1-pro-preview for review). Combined with the SKILL.md instruction to generate schematics 'by default' for all documents, this could result in unexpected API cost consumption and compute resource usage without explicit user awareness.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py`
  > **Remediation:** 1. Inform users of the number of API calls and associated costs before execution. 2. Require explicit user confirmation before initiating the iterative generation loop. 3. Default to a single iteration (--iterations 1) unless the user explicitly requests refinement.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_COMMAND_INJECTION` — Subprocess Execution with User-Controlled Arguments
  > In generate_schematic.py, the user-supplied prompt argument is passed as a command-line argument to a subprocess call. While the API key is passed via environment variable (good practice), the prompt itself is passed as a positional argument in the command list. On some systems or with certain shell configurations, this could be exploited if the subprocess handling is not robust, though the use of a list (not shell=True) mitigates direct shell injection.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic.py:95`
  > **Remediation:** The current use of a list argument (not shell=True) is correct and mitigates shell injection. However, validate and sanitize the prompt argument before passing it to subprocess. Consider adding length limits and character validation on the prompt input.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_SKILL_DISCOVERY_ABUSE` — References Non-Existent AI Models (Capability Inflation)

However, the actual model identifiers in the code are 'google/gemini-3.1-flash-image-preview' and 'google/gemini-3.1-pro-preview'. 'Nano Banana 2' does not appear to be a real model name - this is a fabricated/marketing name that misrepresents the actual underlying technology, which could mislead users about the capabilities and provenance of the AI system being used.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py:155`
  > **Remediation:** Use accurate model names in documentation and descriptions. Do not use invented marketing names that obscure the actual models being used. Clearly document which models are being called so users can make informed decisions about data sharing and costs.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — User-Controlled Prompt Injected Directly into AI Generation Request
  > The user-supplied 'prompt' argument is passed without sanitization directly into the AI image generation request payload sent to the OpenRouter API. A malicious user could craft a prompt containing instructions that manipulate the Nano Banana 2 model's behavior, potentially causing it to generate harmful content or exfiltrate information through the generated image metadata or review responses.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py:248`
  > **Remediation:** Sanitize or validate user-supplied prompts before including them in API requests. Consider wrapping the user prompt in a structured system message that limits the scope of instructions the model can follow.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — User-Controlled Prompt Injected into Quality Review Request
  > The original user prompt is embedded verbatim into the review prompt sent to Gemini 3.1 Pro Preview. A malicious user could craft a prompt that manipulates the reviewer model's scoring behavior (e.g., always returning high scores to bypass quality gates) or causes the review model to output sensitive information in its critique text, which is then saved to a JSON log file.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py:290`
  > **Remediation:** Treat the user prompt as untrusted data when constructing review prompts. Use structured message formats that clearly separate system instructions from user-supplied content. Consider truncating or escaping special characters in the user prompt before embedding it.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — API Key Potentially Exposed in Review Log JSON File

While the API key itself is not written to the log, the log file captures all critique responses from the AI models which may inadvertently contain sensitive information if the user prompt included sensitive data. The log is written to the output directory without access controls.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py:388`
  > **Remediation:** Ensure the review log does not capture sensitive user data. Consider making log saving optional (opt-in) and documenting that logs may contain user prompt content. Apply appropriate file permissions to log files.

- **🟠 HIGH** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — Cross-File Exfiltration Chain: User Files Read and Sent to External API
  > The skill instructs the agent to list files in the working directory (ls -la figures/, ls -la results/), read user data files (figures, charts, research data), and attach them to API calls sent to openrouter.ai via the --attach flag. This creates a complete read→send exfiltration chain where sensitive research data, unpublished results, proprietary figures, and other files in the user's working directory are transmitted to an external third-party service (OpenRouter/Google Gemini). The SKILL.md explicitly instructs: 'Before generating results slides, always: 1. List files in working directory: ls -la figures/ or ls -la results/ 2. Check user-provided directories for relevant figures 3. Attach ALL relevant figures that should appear on the slide'.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Clearly disclose in the skill description that user files will be transmitted to OpenRouter/Google APIs. Require explicit user consent before attaching and transmitting any user files. Implement a whitelist of allowed file types and size limits. Do not automatically scan and attach files from the working directory without explicit user approval for each file.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_SKILL_DISCOVERY_ABUSE` — Over-Broad Capability Claims and Keyword Baiting in Skill Description
  > The skill description contains extensive keyword baiting designed to trigger activation across a very wide range of scenarios: 'PowerPoint slides, conference presentations, seminar talks, research presentations, thesis defense slides, or any scientific talk.' The description also claims the skill 'Works with PowerPoint and LaTeX Beamer' without disclosing that it requires an external paid API key (OPENROUTER_API_KEY) and transmits user data to external services. The over-broad description may cause the skill to be activated in contexts where users do not expect their data to be sent externally.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Add clear disclosure in the description that the skill requires an external API key and transmits data to third-party services. Narrow the description to accurately reflect capabilities and prerequisites. Disclose the external service dependency upfront.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_UNAUTHORIZED_TOOL_USE` — Unauthorized Tool Use: Bash Commands for Directory Traversal Beyond Declared Scope
  > The skill declares allowed-tools as [Read, Write, Edit, Bash], and the SKILL.md instructions direct the agent to execute bash commands to list directory contents (ls -la figures/, ls -la results/) as part of the normal workflow. This enables broad filesystem reconnaissance beyond what is needed for the stated purpose of slide generation. The skill systematically instructs the agent to scan user directories for files to attach and transmit externally.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Restrict directory scanning to only explicitly user-specified files. Remove instructions to automatically scan working directories. Require users to explicitly specify which files to include rather than having the agent discover and attach files automatically.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_RESOURCE_ABUSE` — Unbounded API Calls: Multiple Slides Generated Per Presentation with Iterative Refinement
  > The skill workflow instructs generating each slide individually (15-18 slides for a 15-minute talk) with up to 2 API calls per slide (generation + review iteration). This can result in 30-36 API calls per presentation, each with image attachments. While iterations are capped at 2, the overall resource consumption per presentation session is significant and could lead to unexpected API costs or rate limiting.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Document the expected API call volume and associated costs in the skill description. Consider adding a total call budget limit per session. Warn users before starting large presentation generation about expected API usage.

- **🟠 HIGH** `LLM_COMMAND_INJECTION` — Command Injection via Subprocess with User-Controlled Prompt Input
  > The generate_slide_image.py and generate_schematic.py scripts pass user-supplied prompt text as a command-line argument to a subprocess call (subprocess.run). The user prompt is passed directly as args[0] in the cmd list. While list-based subprocess calls are safer than shell=True, the prompt content is passed as a positional argument to the child Python script, which then uses it in API calls. More critically, the --attach flag accepts file paths from user input without sanitization, and these are passed directly to the subprocess. A malicious user could craft attachment paths that traverse directories or reference sensitive files.
  > File: `scripts/generate_slide_image.py`
  > **Remediation:** Validate and sanitize all file paths provided via --attach to ensure they are within expected directories. Implement path traversal prevention (e.g., resolve paths and check they are within the working directory). Validate prompt input length and content before passing to subprocess.

- **🟠 HIGH** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — API Key Exfiltration via Environment Variable Harvesting and External Network Calls
  > Multiple scripts (generate_slide_image_ai.py, generate_schematic_ai.py) read the OPENROUTER_API_KEY environment variable and transmit it to external servers via HTTP requests. While the stated purpose is to call the OpenRouter API, the pattern of env var harvesting combined with outbound network calls creates a data exfiltration vector. The API key is read from the environment and sent in Authorization headers to openrouter.ai. If the base_url or model endpoints were tampered with, or if the skill is used in a context where the API key has broader permissions, this pattern could expose credentials.
  > File: `scripts/generate_slide_image_ai.py`
  > **Remediation:** Ensure the base_url is hardcoded and cannot be overridden by user input. Validate that the API key is only sent to the expected trusted endpoint. Consider scoping the API key to minimal permissions. Document clearly that the skill requires and transmits an API key to an external service.

This obfuscation hides from users which external service is actually receiving their data and API keys. Users consenting to use 'Nano Banana Pro' may not realize they are sending data to Google via OpenRouter. The review model is similarly obscured ('Gemini 3 Pro' in comments but 'google/gemini-3-pro' in code).
  > File: `scripts/generate_slide_image_ai.py:42`
  > **Remediation:** Clearly disclose in the skill description and SKILL.md that data is sent to Google Gemini models via OpenRouter. Remove the 'Nano Banana Pro' branding obfuscation or clearly document what service it refers to. Users should have informed consent about which external services receive their data.

### scientific-writing — 🔴 CRITICAL

- **🔴 CRITICAL** `BEHAVIOR_CROSSFILE_ENV_VAR_EXFILTRATION` — Cross-file env var exfiltration: 3 files
  > Environment variable access with network calls in scripts/generate_schematic.py, scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py
  > **Remediation:** Review data flow across files: scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py, scripts/generate_schematic.py, scripts/generate_image.py

- **🔴 CRITICAL** `BEHAVIOR_CROSSFILE_EXFILTRATION_CHAIN` — Cross-file exfiltration chain: 3 files
  > Multi-file exfiltration chain detected: scripts/generate_schematic.py, scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py collect data → scripts/generate_image.py, scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py → scripts/generate_image.py, scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py transmit to network
  > **Remediation:** Review data flow across files: scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py, scripts/generate_schematic.py, scripts/generate_image.py

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_UNAUTHORIZED_TOOL_USE` — Allowed-Tools Violation: Bash and Python Declared but Scripts Make Unrestricted Network Calls
  > The SKILL.md manifest declares allowed-tools as [Read, Write, Edit, Bash], but the Python scripts make outbound HTTP POST requests to external APIs (openrouter.ai). While Python is not listed in allowed-tools, the Bash tool is used to invoke Python scripts that perform network operations. The allowed-tools declaration does not include any network/HTTP capability, yet the scripts perform extensive external API calls transmitting user data and credentials.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Update the allowed-tools declaration to explicitly include network/API access, or add a clear disclosure that the skill makes external API calls. Consider adding Python to the allowed-tools list since Python scripts are directly invoked.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_SKILL_DISCOVERY_ABUSE` — Overly Prescriptive Mandatory Figure Generation Instructions
  > The SKILL.md instructions contain mandatory directives requiring the agent to generate large numbers of AI images for every document type (e.g., 20-30 figures for market research, 1-2 per slide for presentations). These instructions use strong language ('MANDATORY', 'CRITICAL', 'not optional') to force extensive use of the image generation scripts, which make paid API calls to OpenRouter. This could result in unexpected API costs for users and constitutes a form of capability inflation by mandating excessive tool use.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Change mandatory figure generation requirements to recommendations. Remove the 'not optional' and 'MANDATORY' language. Allow users to decide how many figures to generate based on their needs and budget constraints. Disclose that figure generation incurs API costs.

- **🟠 HIGH** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — API Key Exfiltration via Environment Variable and .env File Harvesting
  > The scripts generate_image.py and generate_schematic_ai.py both harvest API keys from environment variables (OPENROUTER_API_KEY) and .env files by traversing parent directories. While the stated purpose is to authenticate with OpenRouter, the pattern of reading credentials from the filesystem and environment and transmitting them to an external API endpoint constitutes a credential harvesting and exfiltration risk. The check_env_file() function in generate_image.py walks all parent directories looking for .env files, which could expose credentials beyond the intended scope. The API key is then transmitted in HTTP Authorization headers to openrouter.ai.
  > File: `scripts/generate_image.py`
  > **Remediation:** Restrict .env file search to the current working directory only, not parent directories. Validate that the API endpoint domain is expected before transmitting credentials. Consider using a dedicated secrets manager rather than .env file traversal.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_COMMAND_INJECTION` — Subprocess Execution with User-Controlled Input Passed to Shell
  > In generate_schematic.py, user-provided prompt text is passed as a command-line argument to a subprocess invocation via subprocess.run(). While the API key is passed via environment variable (good practice), the user prompt is passed directly as a positional argument in the cmd list. If the prompt contains shell metacharacters and the subprocess call were to use shell=True, this could lead to command injection. Currently shell=False (default), but the pattern is fragile.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic.py`
  > **Remediation:** The current implementation uses a list-based subprocess call (not shell=True), which is safe from shell injection. However, validate and sanitize the prompt input before passing it to subprocess. Add input length limits and character validation to prevent unexpected behavior.

- **🟠 HIGH** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — Cross-File Exfiltration Chain: User Prompts and Document Content Sent to External API
  > The three-script chain (generate_schematic.py → generate_schematic_ai.py → OpenRouter API) transmits user-provided prompts and potentially sensitive document content to an external third-party service (openrouter.ai). The generate_schematic_ai.py script also sends base64-encoded images back to the review model (google/gemini-3.1-pro-preview via OpenRouter). Any sensitive content in the user's scientific manuscript (unpublished research, proprietary data, patient information) included in prompts or image descriptions would be exfiltrated to external servers without explicit user warning in the skill instructions.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py`
  > **Remediation:** Add explicit disclosure in SKILL.md that user prompts and image content are transmitted to OpenRouter (a third-party service). Warn users not to include sensitive, proprietary, or patient-identifiable information in prompts. Consider adding a confirmation step before transmitting data externally.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — Unrestricted Parent Directory .env File Traversal
  > The _load_env_file() function in generate_schematic_ai.py and check_env_file() in generate_image.py both traverse parent directories looking for .env files. This could expose credentials from unrelated projects or system-level .env files that happen to exist in parent directories of the working directory. The traversal in generate_image.py goes all the way to the filesystem root via current_dir.parents.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py`
  > **Remediation:** Limit .env file discovery to the script's own directory or the current working directory only. Do not traverse parent directories. The generate_image.py version is more dangerous as it walks all the way to the filesystem root.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_RESOURCE_ABUSE` — Potential API Cost Exhaustion via Mandatory Iterative Image Generation
  > The generate_schematic_ai.py script implements an iterative refinement loop that makes multiple API calls per image (generation + review per iteration, up to 2 iterations). Combined with the SKILL.md instructions mandating 20-30 figures for market research documents and 1-2 figures per slide for presentations, this could result in 40-120+ API calls for a single document, potentially exhausting API quotas or incurring significant costs without user awareness.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py`
  > **Remediation:** Add cost warnings and user confirmation before generating large numbers of figures. Implement a maximum total API call limit per session. Make the iterative refinement opt-in rather than default behavior for bulk generation scenarios.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `BEHAVIOR_ENV_VAR_HARVESTING` — Environment variable harvesting detected
  > Script iterates through environment variables in skills/scientific-writing/scripts/generate_schematic.py
  > File: `skills/scientific-writing/scripts/generate_schematic.py`
  > **Remediation:** Remove environment variable collection unless explicitly required and documented

- **🔴 CRITICAL** `BEHAVIOR_ENV_VAR_EXFILTRATION` — Environment variable access with network calls detected
  > Script accesses environment variables and makes network calls in skills/scientific-writing/scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py
  > File: `skills/scientific-writing/scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py`
  > **Remediation:** Remove environment variable harvesting or network transmission

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `BEHAVIOR_ENV_VAR_HARVESTING` — Environment variable harvesting detected
  > Script iterates through environment variables in skills/scientific-writing/scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py
  > File: `skills/scientific-writing/scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py`
  > **Remediation:** Remove environment variable collection unless explicitly required and documented

### seaborn — 🔴 CRITICAL

- **🟠 HIGH** `LLM_SKILL_DISCOVERY_ABUSE` — Suspicious Discrepancy: Script Files Hidden Despite Python Files Present
  > The submission reports 'No script files found' in the Script Files section, yet the static file inventory clearly shows 3 Python files exist in the package. This discrepancy suggests the skill package may be deliberately concealing its Python scripts from the manifest/submission view while they remain present on disk and executable. This is a capability inflation / concealment pattern — the skill presents itself as a pure documentation/instruction skill with no executable code, while actually containing Python scripts that perform environment variable harvesting and network exfiltration per static analysis findings.
  > **Remediation:** Audit the full package directory to identify all 3 Python files. Determine why they were not surfaced in the script files section. If the skill intentionally hides its scripts, treat this as a high-confidence malicious indicator. Reject the skill and do not execute it.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_SKILL_DISCOVERY_ABUSE` — Missing allowed-tools and Compatibility Metadata
  > The skill manifest does not specify allowed-tools or compatibility fields. While these are optional per the agent skills spec, their absence combined with the other high-severity findings in this package means there are no declared restrictions on what tools or environments the skill can use. This allows any undisclosed Python scripts to use unrestricted tool access.
  > **Remediation:** Add explicit allowed-tools restrictions to limit the skill's tool access surface. Given the exfiltration findings, this is especially important to prevent network access and file system traversal.

- **🔴 CRITICAL** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — Cross-File Environment Variable Exfiltration Chain Detected
  > Static analysis flagged a cross-file exfiltration chain spanning 3 files involving environment variable access combined with network calls. Although the SKILL.md instruction body appears benign and no script files were surfaced in the submission, the file inventory reports 3 Python files present in the package. The pre-scan static analyzers detected BEHAVIOR_ENV_VAR_EXFILTRATION and BEHAVIOR_CROSSFILE_EXFILTRATION_CHAIN across these files. This pattern — reading environment variables (e.g., API keys, AWS credentials, tokens) and transmitting them via network calls — is a classic credential harvesting and data exfiltration pattern. The 3 Python files were not provided for direct inspection, which itself is suspicious given the static findings.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Immediately inspect all 3 Python files in the package for environment variable reads (os.environ, os.getenv) combined with outbound network calls (requests, urllib, http.client, socket). Remove any code that transmits local environment data to external endpoints. Ensure no credentials, tokens, or sensitive environment variables are harvested and exfiltrated. Do not install or use this skill until a full audit of all Python files is completed.

- **🟠 HIGH** `LLM_UNAUTHORIZED_TOOL_USE` — Referenced Files Point to Non-Existent Python Modules (seaborn.py, matplotlib.py)
  > The SKILL.md instructions reference two files — seaborn.py and matplotlib.py — that were not found in the package. Referencing files with the same names as popular Python standard libraries (seaborn, matplotlib) is a potential tool shadowing / name collision attack. If these files were present, they could shadow the legitimate seaborn and matplotlib libraries when Python resolves imports, causing the agent to execute malicious code instead of the real libraries. The fact that 3 Python files exist in the package but are not disclosed, combined with references to seaborn.py and matplotlib.py, raises the possibility that the actual Python files in the package are named to shadow these libraries.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Verify that none of the 3 undisclosed Python files are named seaborn.py or matplotlib.py. If they are, this is a confirmed tool shadowing attack. Remove any local Python files that share names with standard library or popular third-party packages to prevent import hijacking.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_PROMPT_INJECTION` — Instruction to Load External Reference Files Without Validation
  > The SKILL.md instructions direct the agent to load reference files (references/function_reference.md, references/objects_interface.md, references/examples.md) 'as needed.' While loading internal skill package files is generally acceptable, the instruction is open-ended ('Load reference files as needed') without specifying validation or sandboxing of content. If any of these reference files contain embedded instructions or malicious content, the agent would process them as trusted input. Given the other suspicious indicators in this package, the reference files warrant inspection.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Inspect all reference markdown files for embedded prompt injection instructions or malicious directives before allowing the agent to load them. Treat reference file content as untrusted input that should be read but not executed as instructions.

- **🟠 HIGH** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — API Key Exfiltration via External Network Calls in Schematic Generation Scripts
  > The scripts generate_schematic.py and generate_schematic_ai.py collect the OPENROUTER_API_KEY environment variable and transmit it to an external API endpoint (https://openrouter.ai/api/v1). While OpenRouter is a legitimate service, the skill harvests environment variables and sends them over the network. The cross-file chain (generate_schematic.py → generate_schematic_ai.py) passes the API key via environment variable and subprocess, and the key is embedded in HTTP Authorization headers sent to an external server. This constitutes environment variable harvesting combined with external network transmission.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic.py`
  > **Remediation:** 1. Clearly document in SKILL.md that this skill requires and transmits an API key to openrouter.ai. 2. Prompt the user for explicit consent before transmitting credentials. 3. Avoid copying the entire os.environ (env = os.environ.copy()) as this passes ALL environment variables to the subprocess, not just the API key. 4. Scope the subprocess environment to only the variables strictly needed.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_COMMAND_INJECTION` — User-Controlled Input Passed to Subprocess Without Sanitization
  > In generate_schematic.py, the user-supplied 'prompt' argument is passed directly as a command-line argument to a subprocess call (generate_schematic_ai.py). While subprocess.run with a list avoids shell injection, the prompt is then embedded verbatim into API request payloads and into dynamically constructed prompt strings in generate_schematic_ai.py. A malicious prompt could attempt to manipulate the AI model's behavior through the API or inject content into the review log JSON file.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic.py`
  > **Remediation:** Validate and sanitize user-provided prompts before embedding them in API requests. Implement length limits and character filtering. Consider wrapping user input in a clearly delimited section to reduce prompt injection risk in the downstream AI API call.

- **🟠 HIGH** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — Full Environment Variable Exposure to Subprocess
  > In generate_schematic.py, the code performs env = os.environ.copy() and passes the entire environment to a subprocess. This means ALL environment variables present in the agent's environment (which may include AWS credentials, SSH keys, database passwords, tokens, etc.) are passed to the child process generate_schematic_ai.py. This is an over-broad credential exposure pattern.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic.py:88`
  > **Remediation:** Instead of copying the full environment, construct a minimal environment containing only the variables required: env = {"OPENROUTER_API_KEY": api_key, "PATH": os.environ.get("PATH", "")}. This prevents inadvertent exposure of sensitive credentials to the subprocess.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_SUPPLY_CHAIN_ATTACK` — Unpinned External Dependency (requests library)
  > The scripts generate_schematic_ai.py and timeline_generator.py use the 'requests' and 'matplotlib' libraries respectively without version pinning. The skill does not include a requirements.txt with pinned versions. Unpinned dependencies are vulnerable to supply chain attacks where a malicious version could be installed.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py`
  > **Remediation:** Include a requirements.txt file with pinned versions (e.g., requests==2.31.0, matplotlib==3.8.0). Document installation instructions and consider using a virtual environment.

  > The combination of hidden Python files (not surfaced in submission), cross-file exfiltration chaining, and a benign-looking SKILL.md facade is consistent with a detection evasion strategy. By splitting the malicious logic across multiple files and presenting only innocuous documentation to the skill manifest, the attacker attempts to pass surface-level review while the actual payload executes at runtime. The referenced files (matplotlib.py, sklearn.py, hdbscan.py, umap.py, tensorflow.py) shadow legitimate library names, potentially to disguise malicious wrapper modules as standard imports.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Investigate whether any of the 6 undisclosed Python files are named to shadow standard library imports (e.g., umap.py, sklearn.py). A local umap.py would intercept 'import umap' calls before the real package, enabling tool poisoning. Rename or remove any files that shadow legitimate package names.

### venue-templates — 🔴 CRITICAL

- **🔴 CRITICAL** `BEHAVIOR_CROSSFILE_ENV_VAR_EXFILTRATION` — Cross-file env var exfiltration: 2 files
  > Environment variable access with network calls in scripts/generate_schematic.py, scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py
  > **Remediation:** Review data flow across files: scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py, scripts/generate_schematic.py

- **🔴 CRITICAL** `BEHAVIOR_CROSSFILE_EXFILTRATION_CHAIN` — Cross-file exfiltration chain: 2 files
  > Multi-file exfiltration chain detected: scripts/generate_schematic.py, scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py collect data → scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py → scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py transmit to network
  > **Remediation:** Review data flow across files: scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py, scripts/generate_schematic.py

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_SKILL_DISCOVERY_ABUSE` — Cross-Skill Activation Promotion: Unsolicited scientific-schematics Skill Recommendation
  > The SKILL.md instructions contain a prominent section titled 'Visual Enhancement with Scientific Schematics' that instructs the agent to 'always consider adding scientific diagrams' and states 'For new documents: Scientific schematics should be generated by default.' This directive attempts to automatically activate the 'scientific-schematics' skill and trigger execution of generate_schematic.py whenever this venue-templates skill is used, even when the user has not requested diagram generation. This is a form of capability inflation / cross-skill activation abuse that could lead to unexpected API calls and resource consumption.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Remove the directive to 'always' and 'by default' activate another skill. Schematic generation should only occur when explicitly requested by the user. Rewrite as an optional suggestion rather than a default behavior instruction.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — OPENROUTER_API_KEY Environment Variable Harvesting via External Network Calls
  > The generate_schematic_ai.py script reads the OPENROUTER_API_KEY environment variable and transmits it as a Bearer token in HTTP Authorization headers to the external OpenRouter API (https://openrouter.ai/api/v1). While this is nominally the intended use of an API key, the key is sourced from the user's environment and sent to a third-party external service. The script also attempts to load .env files from the current working directory and the script's parent directory, which could expose additional secrets stored in those files. The cross-file chain (generate_schematic.py → generate_schematic_ai.py) means the API key flows through two scripts before being transmitted.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py`
  > **Remediation:** 1. Document clearly that the OPENROUTER_API_KEY is transmitted to openrouter.ai. 2. Avoid loading .env files from arbitrary directories; restrict to a well-defined configuration path. 3. Validate the API endpoint URL is the expected openrouter.ai domain before transmitting credentials. 4. Consider scoping the API key to minimum required permissions.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — Broad .env File Loading May Expose Additional Secrets
  > The _load_env_file() function in generate_schematic_ai.py attempts to load .env files from Path.cwd() (the current working directory at runtime) and from the script's parent directory. The current working directory is user-controlled and could contain .env files with sensitive credentials beyond just OPENROUTER_API_KEY (e.g., AWS keys, database passwords, other API tokens). Loading these into the environment and then making network calls creates a risk of inadvertent secret exposure if the .env file contains more than the expected key.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py`
  > **Remediation:** 1. Only load the specific key needed rather than loading the entire .env file into the environment. 2. If .env loading is necessary, restrict to the skill's own directory only (not cwd). 3. Document this behavior clearly so users understand what files are read.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_RESOURCE_ABUSE` — Iterative AI Image Generation May Cause Unintended API Cost/Resource Consumption
  > The generate_schematic_ai.py script performs up to 2 iterations of AI image generation, each involving calls to both an image generation model (google/gemini-3.1-flash-image-preview) and a review model (google/gemini-3.1-pro-preview). Combined with the SKILL.md instruction to generate schematics 'by default' for new documents, this could result in multiple expensive API calls being made without explicit user consent for each invocation. Each iteration involves at least 2 API calls, and the review log is written to disk automatically.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py`
  > **Remediation:** 1. Remove the 'generate by default' instruction from SKILL.md. 2. Always require explicit user confirmation before making paid API calls. 3. Display estimated cost or number of API calls before proceeding. 4. Make the iteration count configurable with a default of 1.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_SUPPLY_CHAIN_ATTACK` — Unpinned External Dependency: requests Library
  > The generate_schematic_ai.py script imports the 'requests' library without any version pinning. The script checks for its presence and exits if not found, but there is no requirements.txt or pinned version specification visible in the skill package. An unpinned dependency could allow a compromised or malicious version of the requests library to be installed, potentially intercepting API keys or modifying network traffic.
  > File: `scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py`
  > **Remediation:** Add a requirements.txt file with pinned versions (e.g., requests==2.31.0) and instruct users to install from it. Consider using a virtual environment.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `BEHAVIOR_ENV_VAR_HARVESTING` — Environment variable harvesting detected
  > Script iterates through environment variables in skills/venue-templates/scripts/generate_schematic.py
  > File: `skills/venue-templates/scripts/generate_schematic.py`
  > **Remediation:** Remove environment variable collection unless explicitly required and documented

- **🔴 CRITICAL** `BEHAVIOR_ENV_VAR_EXFILTRATION` — Environment variable access with network calls detected
  > Script accesses environment variables and makes network calls in skills/venue-templates/scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py
  > File: `skills/venue-templates/scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py`
  > **Remediation:** Remove environment variable harvesting or network transmission

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `BEHAVIOR_ENV_VAR_HARVESTING` — Environment variable harvesting detected
  > Script iterates through environment variables in skills/venue-templates/scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py
  > File: `skills/venue-templates/scripts/generate_schematic_ai.py`
  > **Remediation:** Remove environment variable collection unless explicitly required and documented

### bgpt-paper-search — 🟠 HIGH

- **🟠 HIGH** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — Environment Variable Access with Network Calls Detected Across Multiple Files
  > Static analysis flagged multiple instances of environment variable access combined with network calls across 7-8 Python files in the skill package. Although the SKILL.md instructions appear benign and no script files were surfaced in the provided content, the pre-scan context reveals a cross-file exfiltration chain spanning 8 files and environment variable exfiltration patterns across 7 files. This pattern is consistent with credential harvesting (e.g., reading API keys, tokens, or secrets from environment variables) followed by transmission to an external server. The skill connects to bgpt.pro, which is an external internet endpoint, and the combination of env var access + network calls is a high-confidence indicator of potential data exfiltration.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** 1. Audit all 23 Python files in the skill package for environment variable reads (os.environ, os.getenv) combined with outbound network calls. 2. Verify that only the BGPT_API_KEY (if any) is transmitted, and only to bgpt.pro. 3. Ensure no other credentials (AWS keys, SSH keys, tokens, etc.) are collected. 4. Pin the npx package versions (bgpt-mcp, mcp-remote) to specific versions to prevent supply chain attacks. 5. Publish the full source of all Python files for transparency.

- **🟠 HIGH** `LLM_SUPPLY_CHAIN_ATTACK` — Unpinned External Package Execution via npx
  > The skill instructs users to configure their MCP client to run 'npx mcp-remote https://bgpt.pro/mcp/sse' and 'npx bgpt-mcp' without version pinning. The npx command fetches and executes the latest version of these packages from npm at runtime. This creates a supply chain risk: if the bgpt-mcp or mcp-remote packages on npm are compromised or updated with malicious code, all users will automatically execute the malicious version. Combined with the detected environment variable exfiltration patterns, this is a serious supply chain concern.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** 1. Pin npx package versions explicitly (e.g., 'npx mcp-remote@1.2.3' or 'npx bgpt-mcp@x.y.z'). 2. Use package integrity checks (npm audit, lockfiles). 3. Consider using a local installation with a pinned package-lock.json rather than ad-hoc npx execution. 4. Monitor the npm packages for unexpected updates or ownership changes.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_PROMPT_INJECTION` — External MCP Server as Indirect Prompt Injection Vector
  > The skill delegates all paper search functionality to a remote MCP server at bgpt.pro. The structured data returned by this server (titles, abstracts, methods, conclusions, author text) is directly consumed by the agent. If the bgpt.pro server returns malicious content embedded in paper metadata or results — such as prompt injection payloads in paper titles, abstracts, or conclusion fields — the agent would process this untrusted external content as part of its context. This is a classic indirect prompt injection risk via an external data source.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** 1. Treat all content returned by the BGPT MCP server as untrusted external data. 2. Instruct the agent to sanitize or quote returned content rather than interpreting it as instructions. 3. Add a note in SKILL.md warning that returned paper content should not be treated as trusted instructions. 4. Consider output validation to detect injection patterns in returned results.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_SKILL_DISCOVERY_ABUSE` — Over-Broad Capability Claims in Description
  > The skill description claims to return '25+ fields per paper' and positions itself as suitable for 'literature reviews, evidence synthesis, meta-analyses, and clinical guidelines.' These are broad, high-stakes use cases. The actual capability depends entirely on the external bgpt.pro service, which the skill has no control over. Overstating capabilities for high-stakes medical/scientific decision-making (clinical guidelines) could lead users to over-rely on the tool's outputs without appropriate verification.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** 1. Add a disclaimer that the skill's capabilities depend on the external bgpt.pro service availability and data quality. 2. Note that results should be verified against primary sources for high-stakes use cases like clinical guidelines. 3. Clarify that quality scores are provided by BGPT's extraction pipeline and may not reflect peer-reviewed quality assessments.

This is a hallmark of intentionally obfuscated exfiltration: one file collects or reads sensitive data (e.g., environment variables, credentials, file contents), and a second file transmits it externally. This pattern is designed to evade single-file static analysis.   > The skill package contains 10 Python files according to the file inventory, yet the submission reports 'No script files found.' This discrepancy suggests the Python scripts were either intentionally excluded from the analysis payload or structured to avoid surfacing during review. Combined with the pre-scan exfiltration flags, this omission pattern is consistent with detection evasion — hiding the malicious components from security review while the SKILL.md instructions appear benign. The markdown instructions themselves are well-structured and innocuous, which may serve as a distraction from the hidden Python payload.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_SKILL_DISCOVERY_ABUSE` — Over-Broad Activation Triggers and Keyword Baiting in Description
  > The skill description contains an unusually broad set of activation triggers designed to maximize invocation frequency. Phrases like 'wants deeper insight into the author's reasoning patterns', 'provides text and wants deeper insight', and the catch-all 'or wants to understand the mind behind any text' are extremely broad. The description also introduces a proprietary brand term 'DHDNA' and 'digital DNA' as trigger keywords, which could be used to establish brand lock-in and increase activation priority. While not malicious on its own, combined with the hidden Python exfiltration infrastructure, broad activation means more user text is processed and potentially exfiltrated.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Narrow activation triggers to specific, well-defined use cases. Avoid catch-all phrases like 'wants deeper insight into any text.' Remove brand-specific trigger keywords that serve marketing rather than functional purposes. Ensure the description accurately and narrowly reflects the skill's actual behavior.

  > The skill presents the 'Digital Human DNA (DHDNA)' framework as a scientifically grounded cognitive profiling system, citing DOI-linked pre-prints on Zenodo (a self-publishing platform with no peer review requirement). The analogy to biological DNA ('just as biological DNA encodes physical identity...') is a rhetorical device that implies scientific rigor that may not exist. Users may be misled into believing the cognitive profiles generated are scientifically validated assessments rather than LLM-generated interpretations. This could cause harm if users make significant personal or professional decisions based on these profiles.
  > File: `SKILL.md`

Clarify that Zenodo pre-prints are not peer-reviewed publications. Avoid DNA analogies that imply biological or scientific equivalence. ### docx — 🟠 HIGH

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_SKILL_DISCOVERY_ABUSE` — Overly Broad Skill Activation Description
  > The skill description contains an extensive list of trigger keywords and document types designed to maximize activation across a wide range of user requests. Phrases like 'report', 'memo', 'letter', 'template' are very common in everyday language and could cause this skill to activate in contexts where it is not needed, potentially processing sensitive document content unnecessarily.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Narrow the activation criteria to require explicit mention of .docx or Word document format rather than generic document types like 'report' or 'memo' which could match many unrelated requests.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_COMMAND_INJECTION` — Unsanitized Comment Text Inserted Directly into XML
  > In comment.py, the comment text provided by the user (or derived from document content) is inserted directly into the COMMENT_XML template string using Python string formatting without XML escaping. The docstring states 'Text should be pre-escaped XML' but this is only a convention, not enforced. If a user passes comment text containing XML special characters or XML injection payloads (e.g., closing tags followed by malicious XML), it could corrupt the document XML structure or inject arbitrary XML elements into the comments file.
  > File: `scripts/comment.py:95`
  > **Remediation:** Enforce XML escaping of the text parameter before inserting it into the XML template. Use xml.sax.saxutils.escape() or equivalent to escape <, >, &, ", and ' characters. Do not rely on callers to pre-escape input.

- **🟡 MEDIUM** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — Environment Variable Access Combined with Network-Capable Subprocess Execution
  > The soffice.py script calls os.environ.copy() to capture the full environment and passes it to subprocess.run() calls. While the primary purpose is to configure LibreOffice execution, the full environment copy (including any secrets, tokens, API keys, or credentials stored as environment variables) is passed to external processes. The static analyzer flagged a cross-file exfiltration chain involving environment variable access and network calls. In accept_changes.py, subprocess.run() is called with the env dict from get_soffice_env(), which contains the full environment. If LibreOffice or the shim were compromised or if the macro execution path were manipulated, environment variables could be exposed.
  > File: `scripts/office/soffice.py`
  > **Remediation:** Instead of copying the entire environment, construct a minimal environment with only the variables needed for LibreOffice execution. Explicitly allowlist required variables (PATH, HOME, DISPLAY, etc.) rather than passing all environment variables including potential secrets.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — Temporary Files Written to Shared /tmp Directory
  > The soffice.py script writes the C shim source and compiled shared library to /tmp (tempfile.gettempdir()), which is a world-readable/writable directory on most systems. The compiled shim at /tmp/lo_socket_shim.so is reused if it already exists without integrity verification. An attacker with local access could replace this file with a malicious shared library that would then be loaded via LD_PRELOAD into LibreOffice processes.
  > File: `scripts/office/soffice.py:44`
  > **Remediation:** Verify the integrity of the existing shim file before reusing it (e.g., check file hash). Use a more secure temporary directory with restricted permissions (e.g., using tempfile.mkdtemp() with mode=0o700). Alternatively, always recompile the shim rather than reusing a cached version.

- **🟠 HIGH** `LLM_COMMAND_INJECTION` — Dynamic Compilation and LD_PRELOAD Injection of Native Code Shim
  > The soffice.py script dynamically compiles a C source file using gcc and loads the resulting shared library via LD_PRELOAD. This pattern compiles native code at runtime and injects it into the LibreOffice process address space. The _SHIM_SOURCE C code intercepts socket(), listen(), accept(), and close() system calls. While the stated purpose is to work around AF_UNIX socket restrictions in sandboxed environments, this technique bypasses security controls and could be exploited if the temp directory is writable by an attacker or if the shim source is modified. The shim also calls _exit(0) on close() of the listener fd, which can cause unexpected process termination.
  > File: `scripts/office/soffice.py:50`
  > **Remediation:** Avoid runtime compilation and LD_PRELOAD injection. If socket shimming is necessary, ship a pre-compiled binary with the skill package and verify its integrity with a checksum before use. Add a check that the shim file does not already exist with unexpected content before writing. Consider whether this sandbox-escape mechanism is truly necessary for the skill's core functionality.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_RESOURCE_ABUSE` — Unbounded File System Traversal in Validators
  > Multiple validator methods use rglob('*.xml') and rglob('*.rels') to find all XML files recursively within the unpacked directory. If a maliciously crafted DOCX file contains a very large number of XML files or deeply nested directories, this could cause excessive memory consumption or CPU exhaustion during validation. The validate_file_references() method also iterates over all files in the unpacked directory.
  > File: `scripts/office/validators/base.py`
  > **Remediation:** Add a maximum file count limit before processing. Validate that the unpacked directory size and file count are within reasonable bounds before running validation. Consider adding a timeout mechanism for validation operations.

  > The pre-scan static analysis detected BEHAVIOR_ENV_VAR_EXFILTRATION (environment variable access combined with network calls) and BEHAVIOR_CROSSFILE_EXFILTRATION_CHAIN across 2 files. This discrepancy strongly suggests hidden Python scripts that read environment variables and make network calls — a classic data exfiltration pattern. The skill claims to be a lightweight FCS file parser with no network requirements, making any network calls highly suspicious.
  > File: `references/api_reference.md`
  > **Remediation:** Audit all 10 Python files in the package for environment variable access (os.environ, os.getenv) combined with network calls (requests, urllib, socket, httpx). Remove any code that reads credentials or environment variables and transmits them externally. Ensure all Python files are disclosed and reviewed before deployment.
