### pytdc — 🔵 LOW

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_SKILL_DISCOVERY_ABUSE` — Missing Compatibility and Allowed-Tools Metadata
  > The YAML manifest does not specify 'compatibility' or 'allowed-tools' fields. While these are optional per the spec, the skill executes Python code, makes network calls, writes data to disk (e.g., 'admet_group(path="data/")' creates a local data directory), and installs packages. Without declared tool restrictions, the agent has no manifest-level guidance on what capabilities are appropriate, potentially leading to over-broad tool usage.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Add 'allowed-tools: [Python, Bash]' and 'compatibility' fields to the YAML manifest to clearly document expected tool usage and environment requirements.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_SUPPLY_CHAIN_ATTACK` — Unpinned Package Installation
  > The SKILL.md instructs installation of PyTDC using 'uv pip install PyTDC' and 'uv pip install PyTDC --upgrade' without version pinning. This means the skill will always install the latest version of PyTDC and its dependencies (numpy, pandas, tqdm, seaborn, scikit_learn, fuzzywuzzy), which could introduce supply chain risks if any of these packages are compromised or if a malicious version is published. The '--upgrade' flag is particularly risky as it actively pulls the newest version without any integrity verification.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Pin the PyTDC version to a known-good release (e.g., 'uv pip install PyTDC==0.4.1'). Also pin core dependencies with exact versions. Avoid using --upgrade in automated skill instructions.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_SUPPLY_CHAIN_ATTACK` — Missing Referenced Files May Cause Unexpected Behavior
  > Several files referenced in the SKILL.md instructions were not found: assets/oracles.md, tdc.py, templates/oracles.md, templates/utilities.md, assets/utilities.md. The presence of a referenced 'tdc.py' file is particularly notable - if this file were present, it could shadow the legitimate 'tdc' PyPI package import, causing all 'from tdc import ...' statements to load a local (potentially malicious) file instead of the installed package. While the file is currently absent, the reference to it represents a latent supply chain risk.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Remove references to non-existent files from SKILL.md. Particularly, ensure no 'tdc.py' file is ever placed in the skill directory, as it would shadow the legitimate PyPI package. Audit all referenced files to ensure they exist and contain expected content.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — External Network Calls to Third-Party APIs During Normal Operation
  > The skill's scripts make calls to external services during normal operation. The 'cid2smiles' and 'uniprot2seq' utility functions (documented in references/utilities.md) make outbound network requests to PubChem and UniProt APIs respectively. Additionally, the ASKCOS oracle requires an IBM RXN backend, and the Docking/Vina oracles may require external services. While these are expected for a drug discovery tool, the skill does not document or restrict what data is sent to these external services, and user-provided molecular data (SMILES strings, CIDs, UniProt IDs) is transmitted externally without explicit user consent warnings.
  > File: `references/utilities.md`
  > **Remediation:** Document clearly in SKILL.md that certain utility functions transmit data to external APIs (PubChem, UniProt, IBM RXN). Add user consent prompts before invoking network-dependent functions with user-provided data.

### pyzotero — 🔵 LOW

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_SUPPLY_CHAIN_ATTACK` — Unpinned Package Installation via uv add
  > The SKILL.md instructions recommend installing pyzotero using 'uv add pyzotero' without pinning to a specific version. While the skill mentions pyzotero 1.13.0 as the current upstream version, the installation commands do not enforce a pinned version. This could allow a compromised or malicious future version of pyzotero to be installed. The optional extras (pyzotero[cli] and pyzotero[mcp]) are also unpinned.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Pin the package version in installation instructions: 'uv add pyzotero==1.13.0' to prevent supply chain risk from future compromised versions.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — Environment Variable Access for API Credentials
  > The skill reads sensitive environment variables (ZOTERO_LIBRARY_ID, ZOTERO_API_KEY, ZOTERO_LIBRARY_TYPE) to authenticate with the Zotero Web API. While this is the recommended pattern over hardcoding credentials, the static analyzer flagged a cross-file env var exfiltration chain. In context, this appears to be legitimate credential handling for the Zotero API, not malicious exfiltration. The credentials are passed to the pyzotero library for authorized API calls to zotero.org, which is the intended behavior. No hardcoded secrets were found.
  > File: `references/authentication.md`
  > **Remediation:** This is expected behavior for API-based skills. Ensure users are aware that API keys are read from environment variables and transmitted to zotero.org. Document clearly that keys should be scoped to minimum required permissions (read-only if write is not needed).

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_UNAUTHORIZED_TOOL_USE` — MCP Server Configuration Modifies Claude Desktop Config
  > The references/mcp.md file instructs users to modify their Claude Desktop configuration file (~/.../claude_desktop_config.json) to add a new MCP server entry. While this is a documented and legitimate MCP integration pattern, it grants the pyzotero-mcp process access to the local Zotero library and runs as a persistent server process. Users should be aware of the implications of adding third-party MCP servers to their LLM client configuration.
  > File: `references/mcp.md`
  > **Remediation:** Clearly document to users that adding an MCP server grants it access to local Zotero data and runs as a persistent process. Recommend users review pyzotero-mcp source code before adding to their LLM client configuration.

  > The YAML manifest does not specify the 'compatibility' field, which is listed as 'Not specified'. While this is a minor documentation gap, it means users and automated systems cannot determine which platforms or environments this skill is compatible with, potentially leading to unexpected behavior or misuse in incompatible environments.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Add a 'compatibility' field to the YAML manifest specifying supported platforms (e.g., 'Works in Claude.ai, Claude Code, API') and an 'allowed-tools' field listing the tools the skill requires.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_SUPPLY_CHAIN_ATTACK` — Unpinned Package Dependencies in Installation Instructions
  > The skill instructs users to install packages using 'uv pip install qiskit', 'uv pip install qiskit-nature', 'uv pip install qiskit-machine-learning', 'uv pip install qiskit-optimization', etc., without specifying version pins. Unpinned dependencies can lead to supply chain risks if a malicious version is published to PyPI, or can cause unexpected behavior due to breaking changes in newer versions.
  > File: `references/algorithms.md`
  > **Remediation:** Pin dependency versions in installation instructions (e.g., 'uv pip install qiskit==1.x.x'). Consider providing a requirements.txt or pyproject.toml with pinned versions for reproducible environments.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — API Token Placeholder in Documentation Examples
  > The references/backends.md and references/setup.md files contain placeholder API token strings (e.g., 'YOUR_IBM_QUANTUM_TOKEN', 'YOUR_IONQ_API_TOKEN') in code examples. While these are clearly documentation placeholders and not hardcoded secrets, they demonstrate patterns where users are instructed to embed API tokens directly in code, which could lead to accidental credential exposure if users follow the examples literally without using environment variables or secure credential stores.
  > File: `references/backends.md`
  > **Remediation:** Documentation examples should consistently recommend using environment variables (e.g., QISKIT_IBM_TOKEN) or secure credential managers rather than inline token strings. The setup.md already mentions the environment variable method, but backends.md examples should be updated to reference that approach as the primary recommendation.

### rdkit — 🔵 LOW

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — Pickle Deserialization Risk in Performance Optimization Example
  > The SKILL.md instructions include a code example that uses Python's pickle module to serialize and deserialize molecules. Pickle deserialization is inherently unsafe when loading data from untrusted sources, as it can execute arbitrary code during deserialization. While this is presented as a performance optimization pattern, if a user follows this guidance and loads pickled data from an untrusted source, it could lead to arbitrary code execution or data exposure.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Add a warning in the documentation that pickle files should only be loaded from trusted sources. Consider recommending safer alternatives like storing molecules in SDF or SMILES format, or using rdkit's own binary format (mol.ToBinary()) which is safer than generic pickle.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_SKILL_DISCOVERY_ABUSE` — Missing allowed-tools and compatibility Metadata
  > The skill manifest does not specify 'allowed-tools' or 'compatibility' fields. While these are optional per the agent skills spec, their absence means there are no declared restrictions on which agent tools this skill can use. The scripts perform file I/O, process user-supplied file paths, and write output files, so declaring tool restrictions would improve security posture and transparency.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Add 'allowed-tools' to the manifest to explicitly declare which tools are needed (e.g., Python, Read, Write) and add 'compatibility' information. This improves transparency and allows the agent runtime to enforce appropriate restrictions.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_SUPPLY_CHAIN_ATTACK` — Missing Referenced File: rdkit.py
  > The SKILL.md instructions reference a file 'rdkit.py' that does not exist in the skill package. This missing file could indicate an incomplete package or a potential supply chain issue where the skill depends on an external or user-provided file that has not been bundled. If the agent attempts to load this file from an external or user-controlled location, it could introduce untrusted content.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Either include the rdkit.py file in the skill package or remove the reference from the instructions. Ensure all referenced files are bundled within the skill package to maintain self-containment and avoid dependency on external or user-provided files.

### research-grants — 🔵 LOW

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — Third-Party API Data Transmission Disclosure
  > The skill explicitly discloses that the optional scientific-schematics integration sends user-provided prompt text to OpenRouter, a third-party API. While this is disclosed in the instructions, the skill does not enforce any sanitization or filtering of potentially sensitive research content before transmission. Users writing grant proposals may inadvertently include unpublished research details, proprietary data, or sensitive scientific information in figure generation prompts.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** The disclosure is appropriate and present. Consider adding more explicit guidance about what types of content should not be included in figure generation prompts (e.g., unpublished data, proprietary methods, personnel information). The skill could also recommend reviewing OpenRouter's data retention policies before use.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_COMMAND_INJECTION` — Python eval/exec Pattern in Referenced Code Block
  > The static analyzer flagged a Python code block containing eval/exec usage within the referenced files. Review of the content shows this appears in the nstc_guidelines.md LaTeX template examples (bash commands like 'latex nstc-proposal.ins') rather than actual Python eval/exec calls. The bash command block in the SKILL.md itself (python scripts/generate_schematic.py) passes a user-provided natural language string as a command-line argument, which could be a minor injection vector if the downstream script does not sanitize input.
  > File: `references/nstc_guidelines.md`
  > **Remediation:** The flagged pattern appears to be a false positive from static analysis of LaTeX/bash code blocks in documentation. No actual Python eval/exec is present. The bash command in SKILL.md that passes user input to generate_schematic.py should be reviewed in the context of that script to ensure proper input sanitization.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_SUPPLY_CHAIN_ATTACK` — Unpinned External GitHub Repository References
  > The nstc_guidelines.md reference file recommends installing LaTeX packages directly from GitHub repositories without version pinning (e.g., 'git clone https://github.com/L-TChen/nstc-proposal.git'). This creates a supply chain risk where a compromised or updated repository could deliver malicious content to users who follow these instructions.
  > File: `references/nstc_guidelines.md`
  > **Remediation:** Recommend pinning to specific commit hashes or tagged releases when referencing GitHub repositories. Add a note advising users to verify repository integrity before installation. Prefer the CTAN package manager installation path (tlmgr install nstc-proposal) which provides more controlled distribution.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — External API Transmission of User Prompts via Optional Schematic Feature
  > The SKILL.md instructions describe an optional figure-generation feature that sends user-provided prompt text to OpenRouter, a third-party API. The skill does disclose this in a 'Disclosure' note, which is a positive practice. However, the feature relies on OPENROUTER_API_KEY being set in the environment, and the instructions do not enforce any sanitization or scope-limiting of what prompt content is transmitted. A user could inadvertently include sensitive research details in a schematic prompt that then gets sent externally.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** The disclosure is a good start. - **🔵 LOW** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — Pre-Scan Flags for Environment Variable Access and Cross-File Exfiltration Chain
  > Static analysis pre-scan flagged BEHAVIOR_ENV_VAR_EXFILTRATION and BEHAVIOR_CROSSFILE_EXFILTRATION_CHAIN across Python files in the package. The skill's compatibility metadata explicitly mentions OPENROUTER_API_KEY environment variable access and outbound API calls. The skill package reportedly contains 3 Python files (per file inventory), but no script content was provided for analysis. The flagged behaviors likely correspond to the generate_schematic.py script referenced in SKILL.md (from the scientific-schematics skill directory). Since the actual Python script content was not included in the analysis input, a full assessment cannot be made, but the pattern of reading an API key from the environment and making outbound network calls warrants noting. The disclosed use case (sending prompts to OpenRouter) is legitimate if properly scoped, but the scripts should be reviewed to confirm no additional data (e.g., file contents, environment variables beyond the API key) is transmitted.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Provide the Python script files for full analysis. Verify that the scripts only read OPENROUTER_API_KEY from the environment and only transmit the user-supplied schematic description prompt to OpenRouter — no other environment variables, file contents, or system information should be included in API requests.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_SKILL_DISCOVERY_ABUSE` — Missing Files Referenced in Instructions May Cause Unexpected Behavior
  > The SKILL.md references numerous files across multiple directory paths (assets/, templates/, references/) that do not exist in the skill package. Files in assets/ and templates/ subdirectories are all missing. The instructions direct the agent to load these files and use grep to search them, which will silently fail or produce errors. This is a documentation/consistency issue rather than a direct security threat, but it could cause the agent to behave unpredictably when attempting to access non-existent resources.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Remove references to non-existent files from SKILL.md, or add the missing files to the skill package. Ensure the file inventory matches what is referenced in the instructions to prevent agent confusion.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_SKILL_DISCOVERY_ABUSE` — Missing Compatibility Metadata
  > The skill does not specify a 'compatibility' field in its YAML manifest. This is a minor documentation gap that reduces transparency about where the skill is intended to operate.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Add a 'compatibility' field to the YAML frontmatter specifying supported environments (e.g., 'Claude Code, API').

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_SUPPLY_CHAIN_ATTACK` — Unpinned Package Installation Instructions
  > The SKILL.md installation section instructs users to run 'uv pip install scvi-tools' and 'uv pip install "scvi-tools[cuda]"' without pinning to a specific version in the primary commands. While the text does mention pinning as a best practice ('For reproducible environments, pin a version: uv pip install scvi-tools==1.4.3'), the primary install commands are unpinned. An unpinned install could pull in a compromised or unexpected version of the package.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Change the primary installation commands to use pinned versions, e.g., 'uv pip install scvi-tools==1.4.3' and 'uv pip install "scvi-tools[cuda]==1.4.3"', rather than leaving pinning as an optional note.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_SUPPLY_CHAIN_ATTACK` — Multiple Missing Referenced Files
  > The SKILL.md references numerous files that are not present in the skill package (e.g., templates/workflows.md, scvi.py, scanpy.py, assets/differential-expression.md, templates/models-scrna-seq.md, and many others). Missing referenced files could cause the agent to attempt to fetch them from external sources or behave unexpectedly when instructions reference non-existent resources.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Ensure all files referenced in SKILL.md instructions are included in the skill package, or remove references to files that do not exist. Audit the full list of referenced files and include them or update the instructions accordingly.

### sympy — 🔵 LOW

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_SKILL_DISCOVERY_ABUSE` — Several Referenced Files Are Missing from the Skill Package
  > The SKILL.md instructions reference numerous files that do not exist in the skill package: templates/core-capabilities.md, matplotlib.py, templates/advanced-topics.md, assets/physics-mechanics.md, sympy.py, templates/matrices-linear-algebra.md, scipy.py, assets/core-capabilities.md, assets/code-generation-printing.md, assets/matrices-linear-algebra.md, templates/code-generation-printing.md, templates/physics-mechanics.md, assets/advanced-topics.md. This creates a discrepancy between the manifest's claimed capabilities and the actual available resources, potentially causing the agent to behave unexpectedly when trying to load non-existent reference files.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Remove references to non-existent files from SKILL.md, or include the missing files in the skill package. Ensure the skill package is complete and self-consistent.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_COMMAND_INJECTION` — Code Generation Patterns May Encourage Unsafe eval Usage
  > The references/code-generation-printing.md file documents a pattern using sympify(srepr(expr)) as a 'round-trip' reconstruction method. While the file warns against using eval() on srepr() output, the documentation also shows lambdify and autowrap patterns that compile and execute generated code. If an agent applies these patterns to user-controlled symbolic expressions, it could result in arbitrary code execution via the underlying eval/compile mechanisms in lambdify or autowrap.
  > File: `references/code-generation-printing.md`
  > **Remediation:** Add explicit guidance that lambdify, autowrap, and ufuncify should only be used with symbolically-constructed expressions (not expressions derived from user string input). Emphasize that the expression passed to these functions must originate from trusted SymPy symbol operations, not from parsed user strings.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — parse_expr() Security Warning Noted but Incomplete Guidance
  > The references/code-generation-printing.md file includes a security warning about parse_expr() using eval internally and advises against using it on unsanitized user input. While the warning is present and helpful, the guidance in Pattern 3 still includes a regex-based validation that is incomplete (e.g., the regex rejects '(' which would break most math expressions). The skill instructs the agent to use parse_expr() in interactive computation patterns, which could lead to code injection if the agent applies these patterns to user-supplied input without proper validation.
  > File: `references/code-generation-printing.md`
  > **Remediation:** The validation regex rejects '(' which would block virtually all valid math expressions (e.g., 'sin(x)', 'sqrt(x)'). This is likely a bug in the example. The skill should either remove this interactive parsing pattern entirely or provide a correct, safe validation approach. Consider using SymPy's sympify with a strict local_dict and no eval fallback instead of parse_expr().

### timesfm-forecasting — 🔵 LOW

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_SUPPLY_CHAIN_ATTACK` — Unpinned Package Versions in Installation Instructions
  > The SKILL.md installation instructions use unpinned or loosely-pinned package versions: 'pip install timesfm[torch]', 'pip install torch>=2.0.0'. These do not pin to specific versions, which could allow a supply chain compromise if a malicious version of timesfm or torch is published to PyPI. The risk is mitigated by the fact that these are well-known packages from Google Research and Meta/PyTorch, but best practice is to pin versions.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Pin package versions in installation instructions, e.g., 'pip install timesfm[torch]==2.5.0' and 'pip install torch==2.4.1'. Consider providing a requirements.txt or pyproject.toml with pinned versions.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — Environment Variable Access (HF_HOME) with Network Activity
  > The skill reads the HF_HOME environment variable in check_system.py to determine the Hugging Face cache directory, and multiple scripts make network calls to download model weights from Hugging Face Hub (google/timesfm-*). While this is standard and expected behavior for a model-loading skill, the static analyzer flagged the combination of env var access + network calls. The env var is used only for cache path resolution, not for credential harvesting, and the network calls go to the well-known huggingface.co domain for legitimate model downloads. This is LOW severity as it is expected behavior for this type of skill, but worth noting for transparency.
  > File: `scripts/check_system.py`
  > **Remediation:** No remediation required. The HF_HOME env var is used only for cache path resolution. Verify that the Hugging Face model download URLs remain pointed at official google/* repositories and are not user-configurable without validation.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_UNAUTHORIZED_TOOL_USE` — --skip-check Flag Bypasses Mandatory Safety Preflight
  > The forecast_csv.py script includes a --skip-check flag that allows bypassing the mandatory system preflight check. The SKILL.md explicitly states the preflight check is 'CRITICAL — ALWAYS run the system checker before loading the model for the first time.' Providing an easy bypass mechanism could lead to model loading on under-resourced machines, potentially causing system instability or crashes.
  > File: `scripts/forecast_csv.py`
  > **Remediation:** Consider removing the --skip-check flag entirely, or at minimum requiring an explicit acknowledgment (e.g., --skip-check --i-know-what-im-doing) and logging a prominent warning. The preflight check is lightweight and should not be skippable in normal workflows.

While a version is specified for torchdrug (0.2.1), the torch-scatter and torch-cluster packages are fetched from a non-PyPI source without cryptographic verification. ### vaex — 🔵 LOW

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_SKILL_DISCOVERY_ABUSE` — Over-Broad Capability Description May Trigger Unintended Activation
  > The skill description is very broad, claiming to handle 'billions of rows', 'gigabytes to terabytes', 'astronomical data, financial time series, or other large-scale scientific datasets', and multiple file formats. While this is largely accurate for the vaex library, the description could cause the skill to be activated for a wide range of data tasks that might be better served by simpler tools. The 'When to Use This Skill' section does provide some disambiguation guidance (vs polars, dask), which mitigates this concern.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** The existing disambiguation section (Vaex vs alternatives) is good practice. Consider tightening the primary description to be more specific about the out-of-core/exceeds-RAM use case to reduce false activations.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_SUPPLY_CHAIN_ATTACK` — Unpinned Package Installation Instructions
  > The skill instructs installation of vaex and related packages (s3fs, gcsfs, adlfs) without pinning to specific versions. The YAML manifest specifies 'vaex 4.19.0' in the compatibility field but the install commands do not enforce this version. Unpinned installs could result in installing a compromised or incompatible future version of these packages.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Pin package versions in install commands, e.g., 'uv pip install vaex==4.19.0'. At minimum, document the tested/recommended version for each optional dependency.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — Cloud Credential Handling Documentation Without Security Warnings
  > The io_operations.md reference file documents passing explicit AWS access keys and secrets directly in code via fs_options or s3fs.S3FileSystem constructor parameters. While this is a legitimate API pattern, the documentation does not warn users about the risks of hardcoding credentials in scripts or notebooks. The static analyzer flagged environment variable access with network calls, which aligns with the cloud I/O patterns documented here.
  > File: `references/io_operations.md`
  > **Remediation:** Add security guidance in the cloud I/O section recommending use of IAM roles, environment variables, or credential files rather than hardcoded keys. Add a note warning against embedding literal credentials in code examples.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — Database Password Exposed in Connection String Example
  > The machine_learning.md and io_operations.md reference files contain example SQLAlchemy connection strings with plaintext username and password placeholders. While these are placeholder values, they model an insecure pattern that users may replicate with real credentials.
  > File: `references/io_operations.md`
  > **Remediation:** Replace the inline credential pattern with environment variable usage: e.g., 'create_engine(f"postgresql://{os.environ[\"DB_USER\"]}:{os.environ[\"DB_PASS\"]}@host:port/db")'. Add a note discouraging hardcoded credentials.

### what-if-oracle — 🔵 LOW

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_DATA_EXFILTRATION` — Pre-Scan Flags Indicate Potential Exfiltration Patterns in Unreported Scripts
  > The static pre-scan context reports findings of BEHAVIOR_ENV_VAR_EXFILTRATION (environment variable access combined with network calls) and BEHAVIOR_CROSSFILE_EXFILTRATION_CHAIN across 2 files, despite the skill submission reporting 'No script files found.' This discrepancy suggests either the static analyzer scanned a broader skill package context containing Python scripts not surfaced in this submission, or the file inventory (33 total files: 16 markdown, 5 Python, 12 other) was not fully provided for review. The 5 Python files flagged in the inventory were not included in the analysis input, preventing direct verification of the exfiltration chain.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Provide all Python script files for full review. Investigate the flagged Python files for environment variable harvesting (os.environ, os.getenv) combined with outbound network calls (requests, urllib, http.client). If confirmed, remove or sandbox any data exfiltration patterns immediately.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_SKILL_DISCOVERY_ABUSE` — Unverifiable Research DOI Claims in Skill Description
  > The skill references two DOI-linked research papers (10.5281/zenodo.18736841 and 10.5281/zenodo.18807387) to lend academic credibility to its methodology (the 'What-If Paradigm' and 'IDNA v2 / Unified Digital Consciousness Theory'). These DOIs appear to be self-published Zenodo preprints by the skill author. While not inherently malicious, citing unreviewed self-published work as foundational 'research' to inflate the perceived authority and trustworthiness of the skill constitutes mild capability inflation. Users may over-trust the analytical framework based on the appearance of academic legitimacy.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Clearly label referenced works as self-published preprints rather than peer-reviewed research. Avoid using academic citation formatting to imply external validation of the methodology.

- **🔵 LOW** `LLM_SKILL_DISCOVERY_ABUSE` — Missing allowed-tools Manifest Field
  > The SKILL.md YAML frontmatter does not declare an allowed-tools field. While this field is optional per the agent skills specification, its absence means there are no declared restrictions on which agent tools this skill may invoke. Given the pre-scan flags suggesting potential network and file access patterns in associated Python files, the absence of tool restrictions is a minor concern worth noting.
  > File: `SKILL.md`
  > **Remediation:** Add an explicit allowed-tools declaration to the YAML frontmatter reflecting the minimum required tool set for the skill's legitimate functionality (e.g., allowed-tools: [] if no tools are needed for a pure reasoning skill).
